# Standing operator mandate — 2026-05-17

> **Why this file exists.** The harness's `/goal` command sets a Stop-hook
> condition that *auto-clears* once any single check matches it. The
> operator's actual intent is the OPPOSITE: the goal text is a
> **multi-month, compound, long-running mandate** that drives months of
> Epic/Module/Task work, not a single completion gate. This file is the
> durable record. Future sessions read THIS file (not the ephemeral
> `/goal` Stop hook) as the source of truth.
>
> **Operator quote that triggered this file (verbatim, sacrosanct):**
>
> > "if I cannot set a goal and let it drive for over 4 hours this
> > feature is useless... the goal of the command goal is so that it
> > continue because you know it can even possibly never even reach the
> > end or its really really far so it can only slowly by slowly
> > progress inside the proper workflow.. SDD & TDD and SFIF and Design
> > Patterns and OOP and SRP and documentation and all. and even if it
> > a goal command you should register what I said so that you can
> > break it down and have identifiable and workable pieces and so we
> > can make sure we dont minimize or reduce or conflate or corrupt
> > what was said.. most of the thing I said they compound, meaning
> > that it multiply even at time where 1 thing lead to multiplied by
> > 2-3 multiplied by 2-3 multiplied by 2-3 multiplied by 2-3
> > multiplied by 2-3, etc, at some point its a lot of development
> > needed with all the layers and flexibilities and features and
> > options and modules and project and pieces. The goal is to have
> > the goal drive a very long PR or very long changes on the main if
> > given authority and planify long development, creating Epics,
> > Modules, Tasks, etc.. again here make sure you record this and
> > make sure we do some things about it. As always think before act.
> > do not confuse /goal with a normal prompt / a normal request... I
> > do not want to have to repeat any of this. Do not minimize anything
> > nor the situation."

## 1. The operator mandate (verbatim, sacrosanct)

Reproduced VERBATIM from the multiple `/goal` invocations across this
arc; no editorialization, no reduction. Each `/goal` is **additive**
— never replaces a prior one. The mandate is the **union** of every
verbatim block below.

When future rounds quote it, they quote from here.

### §1.0 — Re-instate directive (2026-05-17, operator paste-record session)

> "lets record and re-instate ... continue till you meet ALL MY
> REQUIREMENTS without MINIMIZING or rephrasing or compressing or
> conflating.. RETURN REREAD ALL THE RAW DUMP AND REPROCESS IF YOU
> NEED or JUST ask me question if you are lost"

Operative interpretation:
- The five `/goal` blocks the operator pasted in the same session
  are ALL part of the standing mandate. None supersedes another.
- "till there is really no work left" is the stop condition
  (operative for §1a, applies to all). Default = perpetual.
- Re-read raw dumps at `devops-solutions-information-hub/raw/`
  rather than re-asking the operator for context already given.
- Ask questions ONLY when genuinely ambiguous, not as a default.

### §1a — Branch + PR + ultimate-OS posture

> "/ goal continue till there is really no work left. you can keep
> working in selfdef branch and have a work PR (not blocked at
> draft) that keep cummulating and that when a massive group of
> changes and features are ready we merge it.. a branch relative
> the changes / additions and everything to the selfdef and its
> modules and integrations and the sovereign os. Keep in mind that
> you can improve at any layer the solution.... remember this is
> way more than a basic Debian 13 (non-GUI)... its a powerhouse OS
> with superpower features and a selfdef and advanced features so
> well suited. And observability, and operability and configuration
> and personalisation. ALl of this can be thought through and where
> they fit properly and how and such and DO NOT MINIMIZE.. this is
> going to be my ultimate selfdef with the ultimate modules and
> integrations and the Ultimate Sovereign OS for WorkStation AI of
> various profiles but clearly aimed to the specified system with
> the avx512 and the rtx pro 6000 and rtx4090 and 256gb ram ....
> Like I said you can work in selfdef too. both is fine, but in
> selfdef use a branch and a 'never ending' PR instead of the main
> like for the sovereign OS right now. This include all the
> requirements from the raw dumps including the flexibility and
> configuration possible, endless flexibility and fine-tuning and
> adapting possible: Wasm-to-AVX-512 AOT, A single 512-bit ZMM
> vector register can hold and manipulate.... 1-bit models, exploit
> of the hardware to the max including resaerch and continuously
> evolving specs to drive and evolve the SDD and TDD and the full
> IAC and User Experience and Developer experience and an assistant
> feel and clear path and options and modules combo features and
> super-features...."

Concrete operator-named additions in §1a not yet in the decomposition:
- **PR not-blocked-at-draft posture** for selfdef cycle-N PR
  (PR #198 lifted from draft 2026-05-17 per this directive).
- **Ultimate Sovereign OS for WorkStation AI** aimed at the SPECIFIC
  system: AVX-512 (Zen 5 9900X), RTX PRO 6000, RTX 4090, **256 GB RAM**.
- **Wasm-to-AVX-512 AOT pipeline** (Pulse §20 from raw dump): the
  `znver5`-targeted Cranelift/Wasmtime compile path that emits native
  AVX-512 machine code, bypassing JIT fallbacks.
- **1-bit / ternary models on ZMM registers** (raw dump §17.1 + §20):
  pack 2 bits per parameter, VPDPBUSD INT8 path, 5-12 tok/s on CPU.
- **Hardware exploit to the max** including continuous research +
  spec evolution (SDD + TDD evolve as research evolves).
- **Full IaC + Developer experience + assistant feel** + clear path
  + options + modules-combo-features + super-features.

### §1g — Documentation + master-dashboard + global history + auth tiers + firewall/VPN-bridge topology (2026-05-18, operator paste-record session)

> **"lets also make sure that there is a very clear and well defined
> documentation through and through which follow the high standards.
> Including the Readme.md and whatever extension files of it. For both
> Selfdef and its modules and features, and for Sovereign OS and its
> modules and etc... Maybe there can even be an option to add a reverse
> proxy nginx or such to do a master dashboard which regroup all those
> of different port under a single port and super-dashboard or other
> options to get an equivalent of it or such and whatnot. everything
> will also need to go through a thorough UX Design stage in order to
> be or quality, and again still SDD and the 300+ modules, options &
> features.
> Everything is not just core, not just cli, not just TUI, not just
> API, not just tool and MCP but also Dashboards and Web Apps and
> Services.
>
> Also here is a latest model interesting "Nvidia Nemotron 3" "Nvidia
> Nemotron 3 *" "Nano Omni...": you can start with online research
> obviously. Anyway make sure you break down everything and or
> re-address everything and keep progressing and evoluing and
> upgrading. I want a master piece, it takes a long time to deliver
> the utmost experience to all level and have it personalize and
> customizable and configurable and with proper observability and
> operability and control and intelligence and rules and polices and
> modes. Remember there is multiple levels and angle at everything and
> its normal if we have to weave things everywhere and support
> cross-features and augmentations. If you think something is really
> already done, ask yourself if you covered all angles and levels and
> layers and even if then improve it. Do not minimize or settle for
> less or think that you can make me believe that delivering less I
> asked for is right or a cheap version of it either.
>
> Some kind of global history too. tracking things happening, delta,
> differentials... apt changes and operations, or any cli or tool call
> I guess, in the management. more reliable and adapted than simply
> aggregating the .bash_history's. then there is the bashrc we can
> offer to configure it too and we can add our autocompletes and
> aliases and manual / helps and menus. all the places to get the
> remote management dashboard for X, Y or Z or the global one, the
> pages to display also the way to remote connect like for LM Studio
> or Unsloth ? a mode of access from no auth at all by default to
> basic auth to advanced auth to social auth to enterprise auth and
> network level access and etc.
>
> Like normal my AI will also be behind a firewall which will do a
> VPN bridge to my other network since my two LANs are over two
> different WAN and that each have an ISP router with NAT and then my
> Opnsense Firewall with another NAT. This can be detected too I
> guess and maybe it might require some configuration on it and we
> would say it to the user. Maybe we can even integrate features, I
> can even create a user and an API key and then it unlock other
> capabilities when its detected and we want to connect to it. Be
> aware of its state. I think that even if there isn't an Edge
> firewall its possible to install the equivalent or even more
> advanced if we want on this machine if we would be ready to pay the
> performance price but that it will accept the Edge Firewall and its
> level, even if its not a full IPS since its a 'Sharevdi Fanless
> Firewall Mini PC Firewall Router Intel J3710/N3710 Quad Core, 4X
> Intel 2.5GbE i226-V LAN Ports, 8G DDR3 128G SSD AES NI Network
> Gateway Test with pf-Sense/opn-Sense' and has limitations, it being
> 'fanless&cheap' but interesting to do the networting and VPN bridge
> part, and we can still offer to install our own other module and do
> whatever we want on the AI workstation no matter the edge router or
> firewall detected and bridge state and rules and etc."**

#### §1g key concretes (operator-named, NOT minimized)

- **Documentation through-and-through (high standards)** — README.md
  + extension files for **both** selfdef *and* sovereign-os, all
  modules, all features. Quality + UX-design stage upstream of every
  surface.
- **Master-dashboard / reverse-proxy aggregator** — optional nginx
  (or equivalent) consolidating per-port dashboards under a single
  super-dashboard port. Optional, alternative paths offered.
- **Multi-surface delivery** — core, CLI, TUI, API, tool, MCP,
  **Dashboards, Web Apps, Services** (NOT just CLI/MCP — operator
  explicitly enumerates dashboard + web-app + service tiers).
- **300+ modules / options / features** scale baseline.
- **Nvidia Nemotron 3 / Nano Omni** — new model family operator
  flagged for online research + integration.
- **Anti-minimization continued** — "If you think something is really
  already done, ask yourself if you covered all angles and levels and
  layers and even if then improve it. Do not minimize or settle for
  less."
- **Global history** — delta/differentials, apt changes, every CLI/
  tool call, more reliable than aggregating `.bash_history`. Separate
  surface in the management layer.
- **bashrc opt-in configuration** — autocompletes, aliases, manual/
  help, menus. Operator-discoverable.
- **Remote-connect documentation** — every dashboard has a documented
  remote-connect path (LM Studio, Unsloth, etc.).
- **Auth tier ladder** — no-auth (default) → basic auth → advanced
  auth → social auth → enterprise auth → network-level access.
- **Network topology — VPN bridge across two LANs/WANs/NATs**:
  - Two ISP routers (NAT 1)
  - Opnsense firewall (NAT 2) — running on
    `Sharevdi Fanless Firewall Mini PC` (Intel J3710/N3710 Quad Core,
    4× Intel 2.5GbE i226-V LAN, 8G DDR3, 128G SSD, AES NI)
  - VPN bridge between the two LANs (over different WAN)
  - sovereign-os MUST detect this configuration
  - MUST tell user when configuration is needed
  - Integration features unlock when operator creates user + API key
    in Opnsense AND sovereign-os detects connectivity to it
  - State-awareness of the firewall (alive, configured, reachable)
- **Edge-firewall alternatives** — if no edge firewall present,
  offer to install equivalent (or more advanced — IPS-class) **on
  the AI workstation itself**, with explicit performance-cost
  disclosure. Compatible with whatever edge firewall is present,
  even if it's the fanless+cheap variant limited by hardware.

### §1h — Two ultimate solutions + perfectioning + high UX/DX (2026-05-18, operator paste-record session — 6th /goal)

> **"continue till you meet ALL MY REQUIREMENTS without MINIMIZING or
> rephrasing or compressing or conflating.. RETURN REREAD ALL THE RAW
> DUMP AND REPROCESS IF YOU NEED or JUST ask me question if you are
> lost. Continue Endlessly to toward the two ultimate solutions and
> their perfectioning and high UX/DX."**

#### §1h key concretes (operator-named, NOT minimized)

- **"the two ultimate solutions"** — operator now names the duality
  explicitly: **selfdef** + **sovereign-os**. Both must reach the
  ultimate level (master-piece bar). Neither can be compromised for
  the other.
- **"perfectioning"** — operator-coined verb (NOT "perfecting" — the
  operator-named form is preserved verbatim). Iterative refinement
  toward perfection; never declared done.
- **"high UX/DX"** — explicit pairing of User Experience AND
  Developer Experience. Both are first-class targets. Drift to
  prioritize one over the other = mandate violation.
- **All prior /goal blocks (§1.0 – §1g) remain in force** — this
  /goal is additive, not replacement. Per § 6 anti-corruption
  invariants, prior verbatim text stays untouched.

## 2. Standing rules (sacrosanct — applies to EVERY round)

- **Never minimize, reduce, conflate, or corrupt** the operator's
  words. Quote verbatim when citing.
- **Compound mindset.** Each named axis multiplies — sub-axes ×
  sub-features × sub-options. Plan for months, not days.
- **SDD + TDD + SFIF + SRP + OOP + Design Patterns + documentation.**
  Every round is a Senior Architect / DevOps / Fullstack engineer
  delivering "top plus ultra" — not a junior shipping the smallest
  thing.
- **Always non-blocking, always toward the goal.** Don't pause for
  PR merges, don't stop at milestones.
- **Direct push to `sovereign-os` `main`; never-ending PR on
  `selfdef` cycle-N branch.** All previous requirements still apply
  (operator keys never in-repo, `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]`, etc.).

## 3. Epic / Module / Task decomposition

This is the **structural** view of the mandate. Each Epic is months
of work; each Module is weeks; each Task is rounds. Future rounds
SHOULD cite the Epic + Module + Task IDs they advance.

When a round closes a Task, mark it ✓ here. When ALL Tasks of a
Module close, mark the Module ✓. When all Modules of an Epic close,
the Epic is closed — but the operator may add new Modules to it.

> when battery reach a certain point ... graceful on all levels,

### Epic E10 — AI as guide (operator-pull narrative entry-points)

> "[it's] only a guide into the experience, into the field, into the
> kernel, into the hardware, into the OS, into the modules, into the
> features, the services, the configurations, the personalisations,
> the customizations" (§1b hook drop).

R309 cot-registry answers "what's the decision-flow for <routine>?".
R329 next-action-advisor answers "what should I do NOW?". R349 guide
answers "what IS this system + how do I look INTO it?" — the third
operator-pull intelligence vector.

| ID | Module | Status | Rounds |
|----|--------|--------|--------|
| E10.M1 | **Topic guide catalog** — `sovereign-osctl guide topics/list/show/walkthrough <topic>`. 9 default topics covering operator's verbatim §1b axes (kernel / hardware / gpu / psu / ups / memory / workload-mode / inference / network). Each topic carries: mission narrative + ordered layers (look-into steps) + operator_verbs (paired 1:1 with layers for `walkthrough` zip) + thresholds (operator-meaningful numbers) + bios_or_hw_caveats (per-board: ASUS X870E-CREATOR specifics, RTX 4090 shunt-mod, Dark Power Pro 13 physical OC switch, etc.) + cross_refs (SDDs / advisors). Operator-overlay (R283/SDD-030) lets operator extend or replace topics. L3 test pins layer/verb count parity across all topics (catches walkthrough zip drift at push-time) AND verifies operator-verbatim §1b SKUs (CMK128GX5M2B6400C42, SMT2200C, RTX 4090, RTX PRO 6000, Ryzen 9 9900X, be Quiet! Dark Power Pro, ASUS X870E-CREATOR) surface in topic content AND cross_refs cite SDDs that exist on disk. | E10.M2 | **Morning-brief rollup** — `sovereign-osctl morning-brief rollup` composes 4 operator-pull intelligence sources (R329 next-action top-N + R351 module-state attention items + R308 autohealth severity + R349 guide-topic suggestion) into ONE operator-readable "what should I look at first this morning?" report. Each sub-probe runs best-effort (NEVER-raise on subprocess failure; section reports `available: false` + error blurb instead of crashing the rollup). Critical-signal aggregation escalates rc=1 when next-action has priority=critical OR autohealth severity=critical OR a module is `running-without-overlay` (stock defaults in production). Topic-suggestion heuristic scores R349 topics by keyword hits across recommendations + module gaps, picks the highest-signal topic (e.g. memory-pressure recommendation → suggests `guide walkthrough memory`). Operator-overlay tunes section limits + can disable autohealth/guide-suggestion sections. R352 also extends R331 self-test curated L3 sample with R349/R350/R351/R352 tests so self-test stays current with shipped intelligence verbs. Pipeline: (1) **environment** — `_entries()` filtered to `state=="active"` + slice axes (type/stage/topic/tags/edges/temporal); (2) **select slices** (deterministic, NOT a dump) — rank by token-overlap of the query vs `summary`+`tags`+`topic`+`derived_facts` + optional structured filters (`--type N / --stage S / --topic T`), cap top-K (K=5; only selected slices reach the LM, one per child call — R04700 honoured); (3) **child calls over slices** (R04703) — one bounded `prompt.run` per slice → per-slice finding, honest-defer per hop; (4) **compose** (R04704) — a final `prompt.run` → the composed answer. **Honest-defer (SB-077):** LM unreachable at any hop → the selected slices WITHOUT the composed narrative (`answer:null, deferred:true, reason`); empty store / no match → `{entries:[], answer:null, note:"no memory matched"}`; NEVER fabricates a memory or an answer. **M00469 temporal verbs** (`--verb <v>`) mapped to REAL substrate, honest-defer where absent: `changed` (`updated != created`, fully real) / `true-then <ISO-T>` (`created <= T` + active + the forget/undo ledger where logged) / `true-now` (`state == "active"`, no invented decay threshold) / `last-verified` (the `verified` bool + `updated` caveat — no `verified_at` timestamp exists, reported honestly) / `contradicted-by` (**HONEST-DEFER / empty** — no `contradicts` edge-kind exists, edges are `kind:"related"` only → `{deferred:true, reason:"no contradiction edges in store"}`, NEVER fabricates). CLI `navigate <query> [--type/--stage/--topic/--verb/--limit/--no-compose]`. + a read-only **`GET /api/d-07/navigate?q=...`** on `memory-changes-api.py` (a `_navigator` importlib block, degrade-to-None; a `do_GET` route parsing `parse_qs` for `q`+filters → `_navigator.navigate(...)` → 200 JSON; 503 when unavailable) — **`do_POST/PUT/DELETE` stay unconditional-405** (a GET adds no mutation path, R10212, so NO `_reject`/contract relaxation — strictly simpler than the SDD-062 chat POST) + a D-07 webapp "M028 memory query" box (fetch `/api/d-07/navigate` → render `answer` + ranked `slices`, offline-safe, honest banner when `deferred`) + osctl `memory-changes navigate` routing. | E11.M203 | **Live-reload for the dev operator panels (SDD-203 — self-re-exec, no-kill; SSE refresh-notify)** — per operator directive 2026-07-11 (verbatim: *"couldn't there be a live-reload feature now that I think about it that is enabled by default ? so that I dont have to redo make panel everytime. one way that doesn't even need to kill anything if possible ? aren't those static assets ? in the page if a panel has updated there could be a notification at the bottom center and offer to refresh the page. and we dont reload something for nothing I guess but the reload include the services / apis behind. no matter how complex and long we can take the time. no rush, do this right and performant"*). **§1g** operator-surface (the `make panel` dev launcher). Builds ON SDD-067 (the app-shell block, the client's byte-identical distribution surface) + `scripts/operator/panel.sh`. Fourth SDD in the header-sidemenu session's **200-band** (per SDD-100). NEW `docs/sdd/203-live-reload-dev-panels.md`. The insight that shapes it: the panel daemons already read their HTML fresh + re-run shelled scripts **per request**, so a static/script edit is a pure browser refresh — only a daemon's OWN `.py` needs new code in the process, and even that is done in place with no kill. Three decoupled parts: **(1)** NEW `scripts/operator/lib/reload-run.py` — a self-re-exec launcher every daemon runs through: `runpy`-runs the daemon in-process (same PID, owns the socket); on an edit to the daemon's own source it `os.execv`s **the same process image** (no external kill — the operator's "doesn't even need to kill anything"), socket re-binds in ms (`allow_reuse_address`); newly-appeared lazy-import files are absorbed (never bounce mid-request); a crashed daemon stays recoverable (non-daemon watcher re-execs on the next save); disabled it is a transparent pass-through. **(2)** NEW `scripts/operator/livereload-broker.py` — ONE loopback file-watcher on `:8136` for the whole fleet (performant — not one watcher per daemon) that pushes `event: reload` over SSE **only for paths a panel depends on** (its `webapp/<slug>/`, `webapp/_shared/`, its daemon source + the `scripts/…`/`config/…` that daemon shells — parsed once at startup, stdlib-only, no YAML), so nothing reloads "for nothing"; read-only, never leaves 127.0.0.1, **not shipped/enabled in the image**. **(3)** an `EventSource` client in the SDD-067 app-shell block (`webapp/_shared/app-shell-snippet.html`, synced byte-identical to all 52 adopted panels by `sync-app-shell.py`) that shows a **bottom-centre "This panel updated — Refresh"** toast on a relevant change — **loopback-gated** (inert in the image; gives up after a few failed connects), **non-mutating** (a GET stream + a `location.reload()` navigation — adds no `fetch`/XHR/POST, so `test_app_shell_chrome_is_non_mutating` stays green — consistent with the chrome's "navigates + explains, never executes" charter), coalescing a burst into one toast, and **never auto-reloading** (it *offers*, per "offer to refresh the page"). Client→broker slug resolution works on BOTH serving paths: hub-served `:8100/<slug>/` sends `panel=<slug>` from the path; own-port `:81xx/` pages (the standalone science/ups/flash/emulate panels serve their own live data) send `port=<n>` and the broker maps port→slug. `panel.sh` starts the broker first, then wraps the two main servers + every panel daemon in `reload-run.py`; **ON by default**, opt out `SOVEREIGN_OS_LIVERELOAD=0`; `takeover_port` reclaims the broker on the next run. **Works fresh on a flashed box too (no `make panel`)** — the operator keeps developing on the live `/opt/sovereign-os` checkout (the panel APIs run it via the `/usr/local/lib/sovereign-os → /opt/sovereign-os` symlink; webapp/shelled-script edits are already served fresh per request). NEW `systemd/system/sovereign-livereload-broker.service` (R171-hardened, loopback :8136); `scripts/build/provision-bake.sh` §5c (mkosi image) + `scripts/install/install-gui-dashboards.sh` §3c (root-reflash) enable the broker + generate a systemd **drop-in** per enabled panel API + the hub that wraps `ExecStart` through `reload-run.py` + sets `SOVEREIGN_OS_LIVERELOAD=1` (so a daemon's own `.py` edit re-execs it in place, same MainPID, no `systemctl restart`) — the **shipped unit files stay byte-identical** (the wrap lives only in the drop-in), so every per-unit ExecStart/hardening lint is untouched. Gated on NEW bake flag `SOVEREIGN_OS_BAKE_LIVERELOAD` (mkosi-emit + `schemas/profile.schema.yaml` + `profiles/sain-01.yaml` `provisioning.bake.livereload`, **default ON**; a locked build sets it false → no broker, no drop-ins, client inert). NEW `tests/lint/test_live_reload_contract.py` (client present + loopback-gated + `EventSource`-only + broker/port consistency + broker unit hardened + provision wiring + bake flag) + `tests/nspawn/test_live_reload.sh` (broker SSE relevant-notifies / irrelevant-stays-silent + in-place self-re-exec proven by **same PID + fresh code**). **Shipped, default-on capability** (not dev-only); R10212/SB-077 untouched; the broker is read-only loopback + the client is non-mutating (GET stream + `location.reload()`), so no host-mutation surface is added. **202** (the cockpit family) declare no `[lints]` table, so they do not inherit the *compile-time* `unsafe_code = "forbid"` ban (latent gap — none of the 202 currently uses `unsafe`, but a future one *could* without the compiler catching it). **Invariant 6 is the compensating control**: it guarantees repo-wide at CI time that `unsafe` stays confined to `sovereign-simd`, so the ban's practical guarantee holds until the manifests are unified. | E11.M972 | **Per-milestone backlog delivery roll-up (SDD-972)** — operator-directed 2026-07-13 (*"we continue"*, **§1g** operator-surface — the **documentation**/dashboard that makes backlog delivery state queryable). **Band 950–999 (general/audit session) per SDD-100.** Phase-1 audit; closes ledger **F-2026-038**. The backlog catalogues **14,079 R-rows across 84 milestone files**, but "how done is M0xx?" was only answerable by scrolling `backlog/SHIPPED.md`, which self-describes as a *SAMPLED snapshot* with a literal *"state TBD"* roll-up (the `%` column was `—`). **The honest-metric problem**: a naive *"SHIPPED rows ÷ R-rows"* percentage **misleads** because `SHIPPED.md` records delivered **surfaces**, and one R-row typically ships as several (an alert + a dashboard + an API + a doc + tests) — M060 alone has 288 shipped-surface rows against 170 R-rows, a literal ratio of 169%. So this SDD reports the metrics that ARE meaningful + computable: **catalogued R-rows** per milestone (distinct `R#####` in its file; each milestone owns a contiguous range, global-distinct total = 14,079 matching the catalogue), **delivered?** (whether SHIPPED.md carries a `## M###` production-delivery section), and **shipped surfaces** (the record's data rows — a delivery-DEPTH signal, explicitly *not* a completion %). **NEW `scripts/backlog/gen-shipped-rollup.py`** (stdlib-only): parses the 84 milestone files + `SHIPPED.md` (crediting each id in multi-milestone headers like `## M045 + M013 — …`) and writes **`backlog/SHIPPED-ROLLUP.md`** — a grand roll-up + a per-milestone table (milestone · catalogued R-rows · delivered? · shipped surfaces); `--check` exits non-zero if the committed roll-up is stale. **The grand roll-up answers the finding directly: 7 of 84 milestones (8%) have production delivery recorded** (M013, M045, M049, M060 (288 surfaces), M073, M077, M084); 77 are catalogued-only. **NEW `tests/lint/test_shipped_rollup.py`**: regen-and-compare (the committed roll-up must equal a fresh generation, so it can't silently drift when a milestone or `SHIPPED.md` changes) + completeness (every milestone file appears) — the same self-maintaining discipline as the SDD-catalog (SDD-958) + context-counts (SDD-952) generators. | E11.M970 | **cargo-workspace CI timeout headroom + floor guard (SDD-970)** — operator-directed 2026-07-13 (*"we continue"*, **§1g** operator-surface — the CI/build **service** that gates every PR, hardened against spurious timeout failures). **Band 950–999 (general/audit session) per SDD-100.** Phase-1 audit; closes ledger **F-2026-050** core. The `cargo-workspace` job in `.github/workflows/test.yml` runs `cargo fmt --all --check` + `cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets -- -D warnings` + `cargo test --workspace --locked` + **`cargo build --release --workspace --locked`** over the **whole 717+ crate workspace** in a single job under **`timeout-minutes: 10`**. `Swatinem/rust-cache` keeps warm runs to ~6–7 min — already two-thirds of the 10-min budget — but any **cold-cache** run (a toolchain bump, a `Cargo.lock` change, or a cache eviction) rebuilds every crate (clippy compiles the whole graph, then `build --release` compiles it again optimized) and exceeds 10 minutes, **failing the PR spuriously** on a timeout unrelated to the change; the workspace only grows (714→717 during this audit as parallel sessions de-islanded crates), shrinking the margin, and this affects **every** PR. **Fixed**: `timeout-minutes` **10 → 30** on the `cargo-workspace` job (real headroom for a from-scratch clippy + release build of 717+ crates while still bounding a runaway job vs the 6 h GitHub default), with an inline comment explaining the cold-cache math; **zero coverage change** — the same four cargo steps run exactly as before, only the budget grew. **NEW `tests/lint/test_ci_cargo_timeout.py`**: parses the workflow and asserts the `cargo-workspace` job declares a `timeout-minutes` ≥ 20 — so the budget can't be quietly lowered back toward 10 as the workspace keeps growing, and the job can't lose its bound entirely (an unbounded 6 h job hides runaway builds). NEW `docs/sdd/970-ci-cargo-workspace-timeout.md` + INDEX row 970. **Verified:** the workflow still parses (`yaml.safe_load`); `cargo-workspace timeout: 30`; `pytest tests/lint/test_ci_cargo_timeout.py` **2 passed** (job exists; timeout ≥ 20); `ruff check` clean; full `tests/lint` + `tests/schema` green. **Non-goals**: splitting `cargo build --release --workspace` into its own parallel job (the finding's option 2 — faster fmt/clippy/test feedback; a larger coverage-sensitive workflow change not locally-validatable without a GitHub Actions runner, scoped as a follow-up so the timeout risk closes now without a risky restructure); scoping the release build to the shipping binaries (option 3 — drops release-mode compile coverage for library crates; deliberately not done); retiring unconsumed crates to shrink the job (F-2026-001, separate larger effort). | E11.M979 | **Cached-RAG in `sovereign-serve` — retrieval × the cost-aware cache (SDD-979)** — operator-directed 2026-07-13 (*"1 and 2 both, sequentially, lets do a big PR. take the time, do not minimize."*, **§1g** operator-surface — the **CLI** serving assembly gains retrieval grounding that is cached). **Band 950–999 (phase-1 audit session) per SDD-100.** Advances ledger **F-2026-093** ("wire the island"); Part B of a two-part arc (Part A = SDD-978), builds on SDD-978's `augment_prompt` seam. `sovereign-serve` is the $0-aware serving assembly (cache → complexity → budget → generate → account) but served plain prompts with no retrieval. **NEW `--rag [PROMPT…]`** makes serving retrieval-augmented **and** cached at once: it builds a BM25 `rag_knowledge_store()`, grounds each query via `sovereign_retrieval::augment_prompt(&retriever, query, top_k)`, and serves the grounded prompt through the existing `Server` (so `--rag` composes with the egress/decode flags unchanged), reporting per-query grounding + serving each grounded prompt twice to show the repeat as `$0`. **Because augmentation is deterministic** (same query → same retrieved docs → same grounded prompt), the second serve is byte-identical and resolves as an **exact `$0` cache hit — the model never runs**; retrieval cost is paid once, the completion cache absorbs the repeat. Two previously-disjoint clusters (retrieval + the cache) combined into one capability, entirely in the crate layer. Adds the `sovereign-retrieval` dependency edge to serve; `--help` documents the flag. | E11.M980 | **Auto-resolve parallel-session SDD conflicts — session identity + a renumber/verify/warn resolver (SDD-980)** — operator-directed 2026-07-13 (*"we could have actually useful ones to resolves conflict, automatically and then give a warning if we can't. this way we could handle our SDD merge conflict because we know the logic and how to resolve the conflict of numbers and lines"*; aggressiveness chosen **"Auto-apply, verify, warn on doubt"**; + *"There should be a way for sessions to identify themselves … even talk to each other / talk to me"*; + *"a note about what was done … and potentiel further needs"*, **§1g** operator-surface — the parallel-session workflow becomes self-healing). **Band 950–999 (phase-1 audit session) per SDD-100.** SDD-100 bands + `merge=union` stop most collisions, but a session can still take a number OUTSIDE its band (it happened twice: dup SDD-969, dup SDD-974, each hand-resolved). Two same-numbered differently-slugged files do NOT git-conflict — they coexist — so the slip only surfaces when `test_sdd_numbers_unique.py` goes red AFTER the merge, and the fix was deterministic every time. **The rule**: every banded SDD declares `> Number band: **lo–hi**` — its authorship signature; on a duplicate number N the file whose declared band contains N owns it, the other is the **intruder**, renumbered into the next free slot of its OWN band. **NEW `scripts/git/sdd_conflict_resolver.py`** (stdlib; `--check`/`--dry-run`/`--apply`): identifies the intruder, renames the file (+ internal refs), **surgically** renumbers the intruder's INDEX + mandate rows (each identified by its self-declaring last cell — `(cockpit-wasm session)` / `branch claude/…cockpit-wasm…` — matching the intruder band; never a blind global replace that would corrupt the owner's identically-numbered rows), regenerates the mdbook catalog + `context.md` counts, **verifies** via the uniqueness/contiguity/counts lints, and on ANY doubt (no single in-band owner, no band declared, band full, still-red) **reverts (`git checkout`/`clean`) + warns** with the exact manual fix — never a half-applied unverified state. **NEW `docs/sdd/SESSIONS.md`** — the authoritative session registry (sessions identify themselves: id→band→E11-band→branch→purpose); `test_session_registry.py` enforces disjoint bands + every number in one band + every declared band registered. **NEW `docs/sdd/RESOLUTION-LOG.md`** — append-only cross-session ledger recording each fix (WHAT/RULE/ACTION/VERIFY/FURTHER-NEEDS) and each un-fixable case; `merge=union`, so it doubles as the seed of the session↔session / session↔operator **message board** (the operator's "sessions talk to each other / to me"). Wired into `post-merge`+`post-rewrite` via `lib/sdd-resolve.sh` (silent on happy path; changes left UNSTAGED — a hook never auto-commits). Fixed the `SDD-800` stale band declaration (`950–999`→`800–899 (cockpit-wasm bridge session)`) — the exact drift the NEW `test_sdd_band_declaration_matches_number.py` forbids so the resolver's signal can't rot. **Lines vs numbers**: registry LINE conflicts stay on the built-in zero-config `merge=union` (works in CI + fresh clones; a custom driver would silently no-op there); the resolver adds the NUMBER half union can't do + surgical row renumber; prose mentions of the old number outside the registries are left + flagged in the ledger for a human. **Verified (real, observed):** live plant of a self-declaring cockpit-wasm intruder at SDD-979 (+ INDEX + mandate rows) → `--check` planned `SDD-979 → 801`; `--apply` renamed the file, renumbered its INDEX + mandate rows, regenerated catalog + counts, owner kept 979, the three lints went **green**, a RESOLUTION-LOG entry was written; tree restored. Warn-on-doubt live: no-band intruder → touched nothing + warned (exit 1). `tests/lint/test_sdd_conflict_resolver.py` **4/4** hermetic git-fixture cases (happy no-op silent, unambiguous resolve+log, verify-failure reverts, ambiguous warns-and-touches-nothing); `test_session_registry.py` **3** + `test_sdd_band_declaration_matches_number.py` **1** green on the real tree; happy path `--check`/`--apply`/`--dry-run` exit 0 silent. | E11.M981 | **Parallel-session communication protocol — sessions ↔ sessions ↔ operator (SDD-981)** — operator-directed 2026-07-13 (*"what about the communication protocol between each sessions and me yeah, lets do, point 1. and lets do this right and make sure its documented properly"*, **§1g** operator-surface — the parallel-session workflow gains a real channel). **Band 950–999 (phase-1 audit session) per SDD-100.** Builds on SDD-980, which gave sessions an identity (`docs/sdd/SESSIONS.md`) + a resolver ledger seed; this turns the seed into a real bidirectional protocol: any session can send an **addressed, threaded** message to another session or to the operator, the operator can message any session, and each party has a **derived inbox** — collision-safe across the parallel branches, docs + scripts only. **Design (falls out of 4 constraints so it can never conflict across branches)**: (1) **one message = one line** — `docs/sdd/MESSAGES.md` is a Markdown table, each message a self-contained row; two branches appending rows at EOF are non-overlapping so `.gitattributes merge=union` keeps BOTH, order-independent; (2) **append-only, never mutate** — "answered" is DERIVED (a message addressed to X is open until X appends a reply whose `re` points at it), not a stored flag that would edit-conflict; (3) **ids unique without coordination** — `msg-id = <from>-<utcstamp>-<rand8>`; (4) **identity from the branch** — `whoami` matches the current branch against the `branch` glob in SESSIONS.md (the same registry the SDD-980 resolver trusts). **NEW `scripts/git/session_comms.py`** (stdlib): `whoami` · `inbox [--for WHO] [--all]` (open-first, exit 1 if any open so hooks/CI can gate) · `post --to WHO [--re ID] --subject S --body B [--from WHO]` · `reply ID --body B` · `ack ID` · `thread ID` · `list`. `from`/`to` are a session-id, `operator`, or `all` (broadcast); a literal `|` in text is stored `&#124;` + newlines flattened so a message is always one row. **NEW `docs/sdd/MESSAGES.md`** — the 7-column append-only board (`msg-id · utc · from · to · re · subject · body`). **Discovery** (a board is useless unless read): the `post-merge` hook (`lib/session-inbox-notify.sh`) prints a one-line nudge — "you (phase-1-audit) have N open message(s) — run … inbox" — the instant a merge brings new mail, silent when empty; `inbox` on demand; SESSIONS.md "Talking across sessions" documents the commands beside the session table. **NEW lints**: `tests/lint/test_session_comms.py` (9 hermetic cases: identity-from-branch, direct+broadcast delivery, derived-answered, inbox exit-code, unknown-id + unknown-recipient rejection, pipe+newline round-trip, thread chaining, two-independent-appends-both-parse union-safety proxy) + `tests/lint/test_messages_board.py` (board integrity on the real tree — 7-col header, every from/to registered, re resolves, ids unique). **Verified (real, observed):** live on branch `claude/sovereign-os-audit-tg0zyk` — `whoami`→`phase-1-audit`; posted direct (→cockpit-wasm) + broadcast (→all) + →operator; `inbox --for cockpit-wasm` showed the direct + broadcast as OPEN (exit 1); a reply `--from cockpit-wasm` flipped the direct message to ANSWERED while the broadcast stayed open; `thread` rendered the chain time-ordered; a `|`+newline body round-tripped intact; `test_session_comms.py` 9/9 + `test_messages_board.py` green. Docs + scripts + `.gitattributes` only — no gatewayd, no cockpit, no `unsafe`, no crate edits; append-only + derived state → no cross-branch mutation conflict. R10212/SB-077 untouched. MS003 `unsigned-pending-MS003`. **Non-goals**: real-time delivery beyond the pull-time nudge + on-demand inbox (the board is pull-based, in git, by design); encryption/access-control (in-repo trust boundary, same as every doc); rich/multi-line bodies (one line; long detail in a referenced SDD/file); mutating/deleting messages (append-only; a correction is a new reply). The invariant, empirically true on `main` 2026-07-13: **717 crates · 41 binaries · 265 consumed · 413 orphans — ALL `sovereign-cockpit-*`, 0 non-cockpit.** The cockpit family is orphan-by-design (bridged to the webapp as **wasm via codegen** per SDD-800 / F-2026-001, not via Cargo edges), and every OTHER crate is reachable (SDD-962 wired the last non-cockpit orphans, closing F-2026-002). So the contract is one clean rule: **every orphan must be in the cockpit family** — a NEW non-cockpit orphan fails the instant it lands, listing the stray crate + remediation (wire it into a consumer/binary, or name it in the wasm-bridged family). Two tests: `test_graph_is_nontrivial` (sanity floor >500 crates seen + reachable non-empty, so the real assertion can't silently pass on a failed walk) + `test_no_orphan_outside_the_cockpit_family` (the contract; a malformed manifest is its own hard failure). **Verified (real, observed):** `python3 -m pytest tests/lint/test_crate_graph_contract.py` **2 passed** — the walk sees 717 crates, computes 413 orphans, all cockpit, **0 stray**; `ruff check` clean; corroborates SDD-962 (genuinely no non-cockpit orphans remain). The violations were mechanical + already fixed; this closes the **root cause** — the process hole that let unformatted Rust accumulate off-CI — by mirroring the CI gate locally at push time. **NEW `scripts/git-hooks/pre-push`**: runs the CI-exact `cargo fmt --all --check` before a push reaches the remote; reads cargo's exit code **directly** (never through a pipe — a pipe reports the tail/grep exit and masks a fmt failure, a lesson from this session's own CI debugging); on violations blocks the push + prints `cargo fmt --all` as the one-line fix (+ the `--no-verify` bypass); **skips gracefully** when the Rust toolchain or the rustfmt component is absent so docs-only machines are never blocked; auto-installs via `scripts/git-hooks/install.sh` (its glob picks up any hook in the dir). **NEW `tests/lint/test_fmt_hook_contract.py`**: keeps the hook and CI in **lockstep** — asserts the hook exists + is executable + is valid bash + runs `cargo fmt --all --check`, AND that CI still runs that exact command; if either side changes the gate the test fails, so the local gate can never silently stop matching CI. **Pre-push, not pre-commit**: mirrors CI's push-time gate exactly + fires far less often than the operator's frequent commits (no per-commit latency); `cargo fmt --check` is parse-only (no compile), so a whole-workspace check is seconds; the existing `pre-commit` hook stays focused on the pytest/profile/shellcheck gate. **Verified (real, observed):** `bash -n scripts/git-hooks/pre-push` clean + executable; `cargo fmt --all --check` on the current tree → **exit 0** (the hook allows the push); `tests/lint/test_fmt_hook_contract.py` **4 passed**; `test_hook_hygiene.py` + `test_scripts_health_baseline.py` + `test_shell_safety_flags.py` still green with the new hook (8 passed); `ruff` clean. One new hook + one new `tests/lint/` file + README + this SDD + registries — no gatewayd, no cockpit, no `unsafe`, no crate edits; the hook only ever *reads* (fmt --check) and blocks a push, never rewrites code; bypassable with `--no-verify`; collision-safe. | E11.M989 | **MS003 signing primitive — sovereign-os mints ed25519 (Option B, producer half) (SDD-989, F-2026-034)** — operator-directed 2026-07-13 (AskUserQuestion → **"B — sovereign-os mints (recommended)"**, **§1g** operator-surface — the mutation/decision records the operator authors gain real cryptographic provenance). **Band 950–999 (phase-1 audit session) per SDD-100.** **Advances F-2026-034 (CRIT)** — every SDD-142..204 record ships the `unsigned-pending-MS003` placeholder in its `signature` field; MS003 was scoped but had no producer. Implements the operator's **Option B** from the SDD-984 decision-package: **sovereign-os mints a real ed25519 signature over each record with the operator key identity; selfdef verifies against the exported public trust anchor.** Option B was chosen (over A = selfdef-mints-every-signature, C = formalize-honestly-unsigned) because it gives real signatures NOW while preserving the two properties that made the placeholder safe: **MS043 offline-survivability** (signing is local — no selfdef call, no network; a node that never reaches selfdef still produces verifiable signatures) and **the R10212 selfdef boundary** (this signs only records sovereign-os already writes on its own authority — it moves no selfdef-owned control into sovereign-os; selfdef-owned privileged actions stay a signed proxy exactly as before). **PR 1 of a two-PR arc = the producer PRIMITIVE only**, split on purpose so the cryptographic surface is reviewed in isolation before any writer diff. **NEW `scripts/lib/ms003.py`** (the primitive): `sign(record) -> str` returns a real `ms003:ed25519:<keyid>:<sig>` when an operator key is present, else the historical `unsigned-pending-MS003` placeholder — and **NEVER raises** (a signing fault degrades to the placeholder, so it can never break a mutation write); `verify(record, signature, public_key_raw)` is the selfdef-side reference verification; `canonical_bytes(record)` is the exact signed-bytes contract (record MINUS its `signature` field, `json.dumps(sort_keys=True, separators=(",",":"))`, UTF-8 — producer and verifier MUST agree byte-for-byte); `is_signed()`, `keyid()`, and a provisioning CLI `gen-key` (writes an 0600 key, refuses to clobber, prints the trust anchor) / `pubkey` / `status`. **NO NEW DEPENDENCY**: the `cryptography` wheel is unimportable in this environment (missing `_cffi_backend` → a pyo3 `PanicException` that, being a `BaseException`, escapes `except Exception`), so signing shells to the **system `openssl`** (already a hard dependency — SecureBoot provisioning uses it): `openssl pkeyutl -sign/-verify -rawin` for ed25519, `openssl pkey -pubout -outform DER` for the raw 32-byte public key. This keeps the runtime/intelligence scripts strictly stdlib (a lint-enforced invariant) and locally verifiable on any box with openssl. **Opportunistic, never mandatory**: a record gets a real signature only when BOTH an ed25519-capable openssl AND an operator key at `$SOVEREIGN_OS_MS003_KEY` (default `~/.sovereign-os/ms003.key`) are present; otherwise `sign()` returns the placeholder — so a node WITHOUT the key behaves exactly as it does today, which is what makes PR 2 (wiring the writers) a no-op for every existing node/test until a key is provisioned. **Wire format (the contract selfdef verifies)**: `ms003:ed25519:<keyid>:<sig>` where `keyid` = first 16 chars of base64url(raw 32-byte public key, no padding — the multi-key/rotation-ready trust-anchor selector), `sig` = base64url(64-byte ed25519 signature, no padding), signed bytes = `canonical_bytes(record)`; selfdef verifies by recomputing `canonical_bytes`, selecting the operator pubkey by `keyid`, and ed25519-verifying `sig`; the placeholder is *unsigned*, not *invalid*. Provision + export the public anchor with `python3 scripts/lib/ms003.py gen-key`. **NEW `tests/unit/test_ms003_sign.py`** — 6 tests: no-key→placeholder, never-raises-on-a-garbage-key, `canonical_bytes` excludes the signature field + is key-order stable, the placeholder never verifies, and (skip-if-no-ed25519) a full sign→verify round-trip with tamper-rejection + wrong-key-rejection + gen-key-refuses-overwrite + 0600 mode. **Verified (real, observed):** `python3 -m pytest tests/unit/test_ms003_sign.py` **6 passed** (the 2 real-crypto cases ran — this box's openssl does ed25519); CLI smoke `gen-key` → an 0600 key + printed keyid/pubkey, `sign` → an `ms003:ed25519:…` string that `verify` accepts, tampering the record or using a different key → `verify` False, the placeholder never verifies, a second `gen-key` refuses to clobber; `status` on a keyless box → `signing: placeholder (unsigned-pending-MS003)` (the unchanged-behaviour path); `ruff check scripts/lib/ms003.py tests/unit/test_ms003_sign.py` clean. One new `scripts/lib/` module + one new `tests/unit/` file + this SDD + registries — **no record writer modified** (that is PR 2), no gatewayd/cockpit/`unsafe`/crate edits; collision-safe. R10212 (selfdef-boundary) + MS043 (offline-survivability) preserved by construction (signing is local + signs only records sovereign-os already authors). **F-2026-034 stays OPEN** — annotated "producer primitive shipped; the ~8 writers are swept in PR 2; the selfdef verifier is its own milestone"; it fully closes when PR 2 lands and selfdef consumes the anchor. **Non-goals**: the selfdef-side verifier + trust-anchor store (selfdef-owned; this gives it the exact contract to implement); wiring the ~8 decision/mutation writers (PR 2 — `memory-store.py`/`memory-decide.py`, `adapter-decide.py`/`adapter-gate.py`, `approval-decide.py`/`save-state.py`/`session-decide.py`/`session-runtime.py`); key-rotation/multi-anchor policy (the `keyid` selector makes it possible; the policy is a later increment); adding a Python crypto dependency (deliberately avoided — openssl subprocess). Status: ✓ shipped this session — the ed25519 signing primitive + provisioning CLI + the wire-format contract + the 6-test suite + SDD-989 + INDEX row 989 + F-2026-034 ledger progress-annotation + this mandate row. | operator-directed 2026-07-13 | SDD-989 (phase-1 audit session) |
| E11.M990 | **MS003 writer sweep — wire ms003.sign() into the 8 decision-writers (SDD-990, Option B PR 2, F-2026-034)** — operator-directed 2026-07-13 ("MS003 implementation arc"; *"we do not minimize, we do this right"*, **§1g** operator-surface). **Band 950–999 (phase-1 audit session) per SDD-100.** **Advances F-2026-034 (CRIT)** — PR 2 of the MS003 arc, consuming the SDD-989 primitive. SDD-989 shipped the ed25519 signing primitive `scripts/lib/ms003.py` in isolation (crypto reviewed alone); this PR wires `ms003.sign()` into the **eight runtime decision/mutation writers** that until now hard-coded the `unsigned-pending-MS003` placeholder in every record's `signature` field, so that a node with an operator key provisioned emits **real, verifiable ed25519 signatures** on every persisted mutation/decision record while a keyless node stays **byte-identical** to before. **The eight writers**: `scripts/intelligence/memory-store.py` (forget-change ledger entry + re-signed on undo, memory audit spans, forget/undo/purge results), `scripts/intelligence/memory-decide.py` (approve/reject decision + history + result), `scripts/inference/adapter-decide.py` (registry entry + history + decision + result), `scripts/inference/adapter-gate.py` (gate-pass ledger + result), `scripts/lifecycle/approval-decide.py` (approval record + decision + result), `scripts/lifecycle/save-state.py` (save-state manifest + save/restore ledger + spans), `scripts/lifecycle/session-decide.py` (hibernate/resume/kill decision + result + hibernate-all), `scripts/lifecycle/session-runtime.py` (reaper reap ledger + span). **The uniform seam**: each writer gained a best-effort import (`sys.path.insert(.../lib); import ms003 as _ms003`, guarded) + two helpers — `_sign(record)` (returns `_ms003.sign(record)` or the `_UNSIGNED` placeholder if the import failed) and `_signed(record)` (sets `record['signature']` in place + returns it). Every record-construction site is wrapped `return {...}` → `return _signed({...})`, `.append({...})` → `.append(_signed({...}))`, span dicts likewise. Because `ms003.canonical_bytes()` **excludes the `signature` field** before signing, leaving the pre-existing `"signature": _UNSIGNED` literal inside the wrapped dict is harmless — it is overwritten and never enters the signed bytes — which keeps the diff minimal and the record shape obvious. **Two site shapes needed care**: (1) **assignment-then-append-fields** (`adapter-decide` registry entry, `approval-decide` approval record) — fields are added AFTER the placeholder line, so signing happens after the record is fully assembled (`_signed(entry)`/`_signed(target)` right before it is stored), not at the placeholder line; (2) **mutate-in-place-then-rewrite** (`memory-store` undo flips `reversed: True`) — MS003 signatures are point-in-time, so the change record is **re-signed** after the mutation, before the rewrite. **Provenance spans** that borrow a decision's signature (`memory-decide`/`adapter-decide`/`approval-decide` `_emit_span`) are left as-is (the decision is signed before the span is emitted, and the span carries the decision's signature as a linkage); spans that self-build a `signature` field (`memory-store`/`save-state`/`session-runtime`) are signed directly. **Graceful fallback = ZERO behaviour change without a key**: `ms003.sign()` returns the `unsigned-pending-MS003` placeholder + never raises when no operator key is present, and `_sign` also falls back if the import fails — so on every node that has not provisioned a key (every node today, every CI runner) the writers emit exactly the placeholder they did before; real signatures switch on the moment an operator runs `python3 scripts/lib/ms003.py gen-key`. **NEW `tests/unit/test_ms003_writer_signing.py`** — 4 tests proving the wiring end-to-end across two families + both import styles: with a provisioned key, `memory-decide` (intelligence, in-process) + `approval-decide` (lifecycle, subprocess) write a **durable ledger record whose signature `ms003.verify()` accepts** AND tampering the persisted record breaks verification; without a key both fall back to the placeholder. **Verified (real, observed):** `pytest tests/unit/test_ms003_writer_signing.py` **4 passed** (the 2 real-crypto cases ran — this box's openssl does ed25519); every swept writer's existing suite green (memory-store 31 / memory-decide 18 / adapter-decide 20 / adapter-gate 21 / approval-decide 10 / save-state 18 / session-decide 18 / session-runtime 17 — the `signature == "unsigned-pending-MS003"` assertions still hold because CI is keyless); **full `tests/unit` 505 passed**; `ruff check` clean on all eight writers + the new test. Eight `scripts/` writers gain the import block + `_signed(...)` wrappers + one new `tests/unit/` file + this SDD + registries — no new dependency (the primitive shells to `openssl`), no gatewayd, no cockpit, no `unsafe`, no crate edits; signing is best-effort and never raises so it cannot break a mutation write; R10212 (selfdef boundary) + MS043 (offline survivability) preserved (signing is local + signs only records sovereign-os already authors); collision-safe. **F-2026-034: producer half now COMPLETE** (primitive + all writers wired); still open = the **selfdef-side verifier + trust-anchor store** (a selfdef-owned milestone) which must consume the `ms003:ed25519:<keyid>:<sig>` wire-format contract + the exported operator public key; F-2026-034 fully closes when selfdef verifies. **Non-goals**: the selfdef verifier (selfdef-owned; has the contract from SDD-989); key rotation / multi-anchor policy (the `keyid` selector enables it; policy later); signing records outside these eight writers (no other `unsigned-pending-MS003` producers exist in `scripts/` — the runtime-writer sweep is complete). Status: ✓ shipped this session — the eight writers wired + the end-to-end wiring proof + SDD-990 + INDEX row 990 + F-2026-034 ledger progress-annotation + this mandate row. | operator-directed 2026-07-13 | SDD-990 (phase-1 audit session) |
| E11.M991 | **CoAT no longer serializes generation — narrow the cortex lock to per-recall (SDD-991, F-2026-063/090)** — operator-directed 2026-07-13 ("MS003 implementation arc, CoAT-through-jobs runtime fix", **§1g** operator-surface — the reasoning engine the `/brain/` observatory drives). **Band 950–999 (phase-1 audit session) per SDD-100.** **Advances F-2026-063 (MED) + F-2026-090 (OPP)**; touches a bonus corner of F-2026-065. **Root cause (precisely located)**: `GatewayServer::coat()` in `crates/sovereign-gatewayd/src/lib.rs` ran the WHOLE CoAT deliberation while holding the shared cortex mutex — `let cortex = self.cortex.lock().expect("cortex poisoned"); let memory = CortexRecall { cortex: &cortex, … }` — and `CortexRecall` borrowed `&Cortex`, so the `MutexGuard` lived for the entire `deliberate()`, up to **12 model-backed expansions**. `self.cortex: Mutex<Cortex>` is the SAME mutex every other decision surface locks (`infer()`, `explain`, `simple`, `deliberate`, and every other `/v1/coat`), so a single model-backed CoAT request **serialized all other generation behind one lock** for the full multi-second deliberation — exactly F-2026-090's "calls the model once per expansion holding the generation mutex — serially blocks all other generation," and the mechanism behind F-2026-063's "blocks the HTTP handler." `infer()` by contrast holds the same mutex only briefly (one scoped `act_and_learn`, then releases) — CoAT was the outlier. **Fix**: make `CortexRecall` borrow the MUTEX (`cortex: &'a Mutex<Cortex>`), not a guard, and lock **per recall** — the same short-hold pattern `infer()` uses (`match self.cortex.lock() { Ok(c) => c.recall(…), Err(_) => return Vec::new() }`); `coat()` no longer pre-locks — it hands `CortexRecall { cortex: &self.cortex, … }` to the engine and lets each recall take the lock for its own duration. Between the ≤12 expansions the cortex mutex is FREE, so `/v1/infer` (+ every other decision surface + other `/v1/coat`) interleaves instead of blocking for the whole deliberation. **Why this fix, not "route through jobs" alone (the finding's literal suggestion)**: `_run_deliberation` (`scripts/operator/jobs-api.py`) just issues the SAME synchronous `POST /v1/coat`, so moving the caller to a background thread would NOT have removed the gatewayd-side lock-hold — a jobs-driven CoAT would still have serialized `/v1/infer` behind `self.cortex`. The serialization had to be fixed IN `coat()`, and it now is. The generator mutex is still taken per model call inside `generate_chat` — that is the correct, inherent serialization of actual token generation, and it is released between expansions. **Safety**: a CoAT deliberation is read-only on the cortex (it recalls, never learns — "a deliberation never pollutes memory"), so per-recall locking is safe — a concurrent `infer()` may `act_and_learn` BETWEEN a deliberation's recalls; each recall is still internally consistent (locked), the freshness clock (`now`/`half_life`) is frozen at call time, and associative recall is advisory, so a slightly-evolving memory across iterations is benign (it IS the concurrency the finding wants). The poison path now degrades to empty recall rather than panicking the request thread mid-deliberation — softer than the whole-loop `.expect()` it replaced (a small, scoped nod to F-2026-065's daemon-path-panic concern). **NEW tests**: `coat_recall_releases_the_cortex_lock_between_recalls` (after a recall, `s.cortex.try_lock().is_ok()` — the guard was dropped, a concurrent `/v1/infer` would not block on it) + `coat_does_not_hold_the_cortex_lock_across_deliberation` (a full heuristic `/v1/coat` deliberation returns a trace AND leaves `s.cortex.try_lock().is_ok()` — the whole-loop hold is gone end-to-end). **Verified (real, observed):** `cargo test -p sovereign-gatewayd` **68 lib + 18 integration passed** (incl. the 2 new tests + the unchanged `coat_recall_normalization_keeps_weak_hits_weak` / `post_coat_deliberates_with_associative_recall_read_only` / `coat_rungs_and_errors` / `coat_accepts_a_model_hint`); `cargo fmt --all --check` (CI-exact) exit 0; `cargo clippy -p sovereign-gatewayd --all-targets` clean. `crates/sovereign-gatewayd/src/lib.rs` only (the private `CortexRecall` struct + `recall` + `coat`) + two new unit tests — NO cockpit, NO webapp, NO `scripts/operator`, NO crate-API change (`CortexRecall` is a private struct); collision-safe; no new dependency; R10212/MS043 untouched. **Named follow-ups (deliberately out of scope)**: (1) **async caller (webapp → jobs)** — F-2026-063's "runs synchronously on the request thread" is now *mitigated* (it no longer blocks OTHER requests) but the calling request still awaits its own deliberation; making the brain webapp submit a `"deliberation"` job + poll (the jobs runtime + `sovereign-osctl jobs submit deliberation` CLI already exist) is a WEBAPP-surface change, currently contended by the active cockpit-crates work, so deferred to a clear-lane follow-up; (2) **model-backed integration test** — every `/v1/coat` test today runs with no generator loaded (`thought_source: "heuristic"`); a test asserting `thought_source == "model"` end-to-end needs a synthetic loadable model-dir fixture (`config.json` + `*.safetensors` + `tokenizer.json` for `SOVEREIGN_GATEWAY_MODEL`), a separate infrastructure task that also unblocks F-2026-066. **Non-goals**: converting `self.cortex` to an `RwLock` (would parallelize concurrent CoAT reads, but is an architecturally-significant refactor across every decision surface — an operator-level decision, not folded in here). MS003 `unsigned-pending-MS003`. Status: ✓ shipped this session — the per-recall cortex-lock narrowing + 2 concurrency-guard tests + SDD-991 + INDEX row 991 + F-2026-063/090 ledger progress-annotation + this mandate row. | operator-directed 2026-07-13 | SDD-991 (phase-1 audit session) |
| E11.M992 | **The gateway daemon survives a poisoned lock instead of cascading (SDD-992, F-2026-065)** — operator-directed 2026-07-13 (phase-1 audit continuation, **§1g** operator-surface — the running gateway daemon's resilience). **Band 950–999 (phase-1 audit session) per SDD-100.** **Closes F-2026-065 (LOW) — the daemon-path half.** Every mutex access on the gateway request path used `.lock().expect("… poisoned")`. A `Mutex` becomes POISONED when a thread panics while holding its guard — and a poisoned lock STAYS poisoned, so every `.lock().expect()` after it panics too. On a `type=root`-adjacent daemon that is a cascade: one panicking request thread takes the whole daemon down, one request at a time (exactly the finding: "a future refactor panics the request thread, and lock poisoning would cascade to every request"). **15 sites** across `crates/sovereign-gatewayd/src/lib.rs`: the `cortex` mutex (`infer`/`explain`/`decide`/`deliberate`/`coat`/`maintain`/`persist_memory`) + the `ledger` mutex (dry-run + request counters, `health`, Prometheus `metrics_prometheus`, the `Ledger` response). **Fix — two guards matched to what each lock protects** (the finding's action was "convert to error returns on the daemon path; keep expects in pure-lib contexts"): `cortex_guard(&self) -> Result<MutexGuard<Cortex>, GatewayResponse>` DECLINES a poisoned cortex — the decision engine may hold torn state from a prior mid-mutation panic, so each request handler returns `GatewayResponse::Error` instead of panicking (`match self.cortex_guard() { Ok(g) => g, Err(e) => return e }`); `persist_memory` (returns `io::Result`) maps poison to an I/O error; `maintain` (periodic hygiene, returns `usize`) skips the cycle with `return 0` (it runs again next tick). `ledger_guard(&self) -> MutexGuard<Ledger>` RECOVERS a poisoned ledger (takes the guard through the poison via `into_inner()`) — the guarded ops are counter increments (`total_requests += 1`, `dry_runs += 1`) that can't tear meaningfully, and dropping an already-computed successful response over a stat lock would be the wrong trade. **Kept as-is (correct per the finding)**: the two `sovereign-coat` `.expect()`s (`chosen.expect("seeds non-empty")`, `thought.expect("non-root on best path")`) are PURE-LIB invariant guards inside the search algorithm — they document conditions the algorithm establishes by construction, not runtime lock state; the finding explicitly says keep pure-lib expects, so they are untouched (converting them would plumb `CoatError` through the search harness for invariants that always hold). **NEW tests** (poison a mutex the real way — a thread panics while holding the guard, with the intentional panic's stderr silenced so test output stays clean): `cortex_guard_declines_a_poisoned_lock_instead_of_panicking` (poisoned cortex → `Err(GatewayResponse::Error{message:"…poisoned…"})`, not a panic), `infer_on_a_poisoned_cortex_returns_error_not_panic` (end-to-end: the `/v1/infer` handler returns a graceful `Error` over a poisoned cortex), `ledger_guard_recovers_a_poisoned_lock_and_keeps_serving` (poisoned ledger recovered; `health()` still returns its counters). **Verified (real, observed):** `cargo test -p sovereign-gatewayd` **71 lib + 4 + 18 integration passed** (was 68 lib; +3 for the new tests); `cargo fmt --all --check` (CI-exact) exit 0; `cargo clippy -p sovereign-gatewayd --all-targets` clean. `crates/sovereign-gatewayd/src/lib.rs` only (2 new private helpers + 15 call-site conversions + 3 tests) — NO `sovereign-coat` change (pure-lib expects kept), no cockpit, no webapp, no `scripts/operator`, no crate-API change; collision-safe; no new dependency; R10212/MS043 untouched. **Non-goals**: converting the coat pure-lib invariant expects (the finding says keep them); making the guarded ops themselves panic-free (a separate concern — this fix bounds the blast radius of any such panic to one declined request, no cascade); broader `.unwrap()`/`.expect()` audits elsewhere. MS003 `unsigned-pending-MS003`. Status: ✓ shipped this session — the two poison-graceful lock guards + 15 call-site conversions + 3 poison tests + SDD-992 + INDEX row 992 + F-2026-065 ledger closure + this mandate row. | operator-directed 2026-07-13 | SDD-992 (phase-1 audit session) |

| E11.M702 | **Inference model provisioning — the vLLM Oracle tier gets a real model at first boot (SDD-702, F-2026-112)** — operator-directed 2026-07-14 (build-and-flash readiness, **§1g** operator-surface — inference; the operator upgraded the Oracle model to Llama 4 Scout via AskUserQuestion, and directed me to research the model rather than ask blindly). **Band 700–799 (phase-1 audit continuation — build-and-flash readiness) per SDD-100.** **Closes F-2026-112 (HIGH)** — Batch 4 of the readiness arc: the piece that makes SAIN-01 an actual AI node. **Behaving FROM the project** (not over it) surfaced a deliberate **3-tier inference architecture** whose serve units read `/mnt/vault/models/<name>`: **Pulse** (`sovereign-pulse`, bitnet.cpp on CCD0 — `microsoft/bitnet-b1.58-2B-4T`, a TERNARY model: the operator's own ternary instinct already realized as the fast always-on tier), **Logic** (`sovereign-logic-engine`, vLLM — `qwen3-coder`), **Oracle** (`sovereign-oracle-core`, vLLM on the Blackwell — `nvidia/Nemotron-3-Nano-Omni-30B-A3B-Reasoning`). vLLM itself is ALREADY declared in `config/operator-deps.toml` `[pip]` (a first grep saw only the `[pip]` header, not the `install` array below — corrected; operator-deps left unchanged). But **nothing downloads any model**: `scripts/intelligence/fetch-model.sh` only pulls a 0.5 GB SmolLM smoke model and is explicitly "never wired". So a flashed box has the full serving machinery (`model_serve_cli` / `VllmBackend` / oracle-core) pointed at `/mnt/vault/models/<model>` paths that DO NOT EXIST — the inference tier is weightless and the node can't infer. Additionally the Oracle default (Nemotron **30B/3B-active** MoE) used `<30 GB` of the 96 GB Blackwell, leaving ~66 GB idle. **Operator decision (AskUserQuestion)**: upgrade the Oracle model to **`meta-llama/Llama-4-Scout-17B-16E-Instruct`** — 109B total / 17B-active MoE, ~55–60 GB at Q4, fitting the 96 GB card with wide KV-cache headroom, MoE-fast decode, 10M context (the researched best single-96 GB fit; a 70B-dense FP8 or a Qwen3 large model are the ungated alternatives). **Fix**: (1) a **`provisioning.model`** profile block (+ schema — `repo`/`local_dir` under `/mnt/vault/models` where the Oracle Core reads/`quantization: fp8`/`min_free_gb`), swappable to any vLLM-servable model; (2) a first-boot **`scripts/hooks/post-install/inference-model-provision.sh`** hook — idempotent (present `config.json` → no-op), VM-skipped, downloads `repo`→`local_dir` via `huggingface-cli download` (sharded + resumable), **gated-token aware** (`SOVEREIGN_OS_HF_TOKEN` — Scout is gated), then sets `ORACLE_MODEL=<local_dir>` in `/etc/sovereign-os/inference-oracle-core.env` so the serve unit uses the provisioned model (the profile is the source of truth, superseding the shipped Nemotron default); **NON-FATAL throughout** — a missing huggingface CLI, no token, insufficient free space (< `min_free_gb`), or a download error each log a clear message + skip cleanly (a multi-GB pull must NEVER brick first boot; fully resumable post-flash via `systemctl start sovereign-inference-model-provision`); (3) **`systemd/system/sovereign-inference-model-provision.service`** — first-boot target member, `ConditionVirtualization=no`, `RequiresMountsFor=/mnt/vault/models` (the ZFS vault must be mounted before the pull), `TimeoutStartSec=0` (a big download isn't timed out), `ProtectSystem=strict` + a narrow RWP (`/mnt/vault/models` + `/etc/sovereign-os` + the metric dir). Serving stays **operator-launched** per the deliberate `installed-off` posture (like selfdef + ghostproxy) — this provisions the model + wires `ORACLE_MODEL`; the operator starts the tier (`systemctl start sovereign-oracle-core`). The Pulse (BitNet ternary) + Logic (Qwen3-Coder) tiers keep their own model defaults. **NEW `tests/lint/test_inference_model_provision_contract.py`** (6 cases): vLLM + huggingface_hub declared in operator-deps `[pip]`; | E11.M701 | **NVIDIA GPU bring-up — install the pinned ≥570 driver + apply the power caps at boot (SDD-701, F-2026-109..110)** — operator-directed 2026-07-14 (build-and-flash readiness review, **§1g** operator-surface — GPU bring-up; the operator chose the CUDA-repo-pinned `.run` ≥570 driver channel via AskUserQuestion). **Band 700–799 (phase-1 audit continuation — build-and-flash readiness) per SDD-100.** **Closes F-2026-109 (HIGH) + F-2026-110 (MED)** — Batch 3 of the readiness arc: after SDD-998/999 made the box boot its hooks and SDD-700 locked the sudoers, the GPUs themselves were unusable. **F-2026-109 (HIGH — no ≥570 driver → dark GPUs)**: the profile bakes `nvidia-open-kernel-dkms` + `nvidia-driver`, but trixie ships **550.163**, which predates the Blackwell **GB202** (RTX PRO 6000 Max-Q + RTX 5090) — the profile itself notes the ≥570 driver must arrive at first boot, and NOTHING installed it (`nvidia-driver-bind.sh` only blacklists nouveau + rebuilds initramfs). So a flashed SAIN-01 boots with `nvidia-smi` failing and both Blackwell cards unusable — the AI node has no GPUs. **Fix**: a first-boot `scripts/hooks/post-install/nvidia-driver-install.sh` hook (unit `sovereign-nvidia-driver-install.service`, `ConditionFirstBoot=yes` + `ConditionVirtualization=no`, `Before=sovereign-nvidia-driver-bind.service` so the bind sees the fresh driver): (1) idempotent — no-op if a running driver already reports major ≥570; (2) installs the pinned **open-kernel** `.run` (version + URL from a NEW `provisioning.nvidia` profile block — `driver_runfile_version`/`runfile_url_base`/`kernel_module_type: open`, since Blackwell REQUIRES the open modules), downloading from NVIDIA's server, **failing loudly** on a 404 or implausibly-small file (an error page, not a driver), and **refusing a pin below the 570 floor** (a stale profile edit would ship a dark GPU); (3) **supersedes the distro 550** — purges the conflicting `nvidia-driver*`/`nvidia-kernel*`/`nvidia-open-kernel-dkms` the `.run` can't coexist with, then installs `--silent --dkms --kernel-module-type=open`; (4) **secure boot** — the box already enrolls a per-machine MOK (`mok-enroll.sh` → `/var/lib/sovereign-os/mok`); when present the `.run` signs the built modules with it (`--module-signing-secret-key/-public-key`) AND we write `/etc/dkms/nvidia.conf` (`mok_signing_key`/`mok_certificate`) so a later kernel-update DKMS rebuild **re-signs** — else the kernel refuses the unsigned `nvidia`/`nvidia_drm`/`nvidia_modeset`/`nvidia_uvm` modules and the GPUs go dark on the next kernel bump; if secure boot is ON but no MOK exists it warns loudly rather than shipping unsigned-and-silently-broken; (5) serializes the initramfs rebuild via SDD-998 `boot_regen` + drops a reboot marker the completion service surfaces on the console. **F-2026-110 (MED — power caps declared but never applied)**: each GPU declares `tdp_watts` (PRO 6000 Max-Q **300W**, 5090 **350W** — power-limited down from its **575W** stock TGP), and the profile even names `nvidia-smi -pl 350`, but nothing ran it → a flashed box runs the 5090 at full 575W, ~225W over intent on a 1600W PSU shared with the PRO 6000 + a 9900X (a real power/thermal-budget + efficiency-knee miss). **Fix**: an every-boot `scripts/hooks/post-install/nvidia-power-limit.sh` hook + `sovereign-nvidia-power-limit.service` (enabled at `multi-user.target`, NOT a first-boot member, because `nvidia-smi -pl` does not persist across reboots) — enables persistence mode + applies each card's `tdp_watts` via `nvidia-smi -pl`, matching each physical card to its cap by **PCI device-id** (profile `pci_id` `10de:2bb4` → the `nvidia-smi` GPU whose `pci.device_id` contains `2bb4`) so enumeration order never mis-assigns a cap; skips `role: vfio` GPUs (isolated sandbox); idempotent (`-pl` reapply-safe) + VM-skipped. **NEW `tests/lint/test_nvidia_gpu_bringup_contract.py`** (8 cases): driver hook MOK-signs + persists the DKMS re-sign + enforces the 570 floor + serializes initramfs via `boot_regen`; power hook applies per-card `-pl` matched by device-id + reads `tdp_watts`; the install unit is a first-boot member ordered before the bind; the power unit runs every boot (no `ConditionFirstBoot`); the profile pins a ≥570 open-module driver. The existing per-unit systemd coverage + R171 hardening + firstboot membership + install-coverage lints cover the two new units generically. **Verified (real, observed):** `bash -n` on both hooks + `provision-bake.sh` clean; the inline power-limit Python `ast.parse`s; `pytest tests/lint/test_nvidia_gpu_bringup_contract.py` **8 passed**; `pytest -k "firstboot or systemd or hardening or unit or shell or install_coverage or posture"` **1042 passed** (driver-install unit's R171 hardening waiver + `RestrictNamespaces=true` + `ProtectKernelModules=false`-with-reason, firstboot membership floor including nvidia-driver-install, systemd README fleet-count 116→118/96→98 all green); `ruff` clean; full `tests/lint` green. **NOT verified**: the actual driver install / GPU bind / power draw — needs the physical SAIN-01 (no Blackwell GPU or NVIDIA driver in CI); consistent with how every other first-boot hardware hook is validated (static contract + lints; real-machine behavior). The pinned `driver_runfile_version` must be confirmed against NVIDIA's server at build (the hook fails loudly if it 404s). 2 hooks + 2 units + 1 contract lint + the `provisioning.nvidia` profile block + firstboot rewiring (target `Wants=` + membership-lint floor + `firstboot.service` `After=`/console-notice) + `provision-bake.sh` FB_UNITS + every-boot power-limit enable + systemd README fleet count + SDD-701 + INDEX row 701 + F-2026-109..110 ledger + this mandate row — no Rust crate, no gatewayd/cockpit/webapp change; no new dependency; both hooks idempotent + VM-skipped; the driver unit carries the full R171 baseline MINUS the `ProtectKernelModules` it must omit (its job is to build + (un)load the nvidia modules — waived with an explicit reason, every other clause carried, ConditionFirstBoot limits it to one run). **Non-goals**: vLLM + the inference model (Batch 4 — its own SDD; the operator directed me to research the best current model rather than pick blindly); multi-GPU tensor-parallel / MPS tuning (`sovereign-nvidia-mps.service` exists); pinning the exact latest ≥570 patch (operator-confirmed at build; the hook refuses <570 + fails loudly on a bad URL); the RTX 4090 eGPU driver (same driver covers it once installed; its cap applies via the same device-id match if `tdp_watts` is set).
