| E11.M700 | **Operator sudoers — risk-tier the OPS grants + lock them against privilege-escalation drift (SDD-700, F-2026-107..108)** — operator-directed 2026-07-14 (build-and-flash readiness review, **§1g** operator-surface — *"everything that needs to be in the sudoer are there too?"*). **Band 700–799 (phase-1 audit continuation — build-and-flash readiness) per SDD-100** (the 950–999 audit band filled — SDD-998/999 took its last slots — so this arc continues in the next free disjoint block; band row added to SDD-100 + docs/sdd/README.md). **Closes F-2026-107 (MED) + F-2026-108 (LOW).** The right answer to "are the needed commands in the sudoer" has two halves — *are they granted?* (yes: diagnostics + image-verify + the cockpit control verbs) and, the half nothing guarded, *are ONLY the right things granted, and can a dangerous one drift in?* **F-2026-107 (MED — the OPS bucket had no coverage lint + no privesc guard)**: `scripts/operator/operator-sudoers.sh` installs a scoped NOPASSWD drop-in (the panels + the AI agent run as the operator user). Its per-verb `SOVEREIGN_OS_COCKPIT` alias is lockstep-linted (kept in sync with the control registry, selfdef/perimeter proven absent by `test_cockpit_action_exec_sudoers.py`) — WELL-guarded. But the OPS bucket (one opaque `SOVEREIGN_OS_OPS` alias built from the `DIAG` read-only-probes / `IMAGE` loop-mount / `PROC` kill shell arrays) had NONE: `test_operator_sudoers.py` only asserted it wasn't `NOPASSWD: ALL` and that entries were absolute paths, so a single edit adding `bash`/`dd`/`systemctl`/`tee`/`chmod`/`python` to the `DIAG` array would silently turn the "scoped, reviewable, never-ALL" drop-in into a NOPASSWD ROOT SHELL — root-equivalent — and every lint would still pass. **Fix — two moves**: (1) **risk-tier** the one alias into three so the `/etc/sudoers.d` file self-documents danger — `SOVEREIGN_OS_DIAG` (read-only hardware/system diagnostics, low risk), `SOVEREIGN_OS_IMAGE` (**HIGH-RISK**: loop-mount + inspect a built image before flashing), `SOVEREIGN_OS_PROC` (process control — reclaim a prior root-owned panel port); the grant line lists only scoped aliases, never a raw command; a new `_resolve_bucket` helper resolves each tier's names → deduped absolute paths. (2) **lock + guard** in `test_operator_sudoers.py`: each tier's command set must EQUAL the reviewed set (`EXPECTED_DIAG`/`EXPECTED_IMAGE`/`EXPECTED_PROC` — the lockstep drift-lock, so a new grant is a deliberate reviewed change to the lint, mirroring the cockpit alias's discipline) AND no tier may contain any of a curated privilege-escalation denylist (shells `bash`/`sh`/`zsh`…, interpreters `python`/`perl`/`ruby`/`node`…, `dd`/`tee`/`cp`/`mv`/`install`/`ln`/`chmod`/`chown`/`chroot`/`mknod`/`nsenter`, `systemctl`/`service`/`init`, package managers, pagers/editors with shell escapes, `find`/`tar`/`rsync`/`cpio` with command-exec flags, `su`/`sudo`/`passwd`/`useradd`/`visudo` — defense-in-depth even if BOTH the script and `EXPECTED_*` were edited together). The image loop-mount primitives (`losetup`/`mount`/`umount`) stay — they are the reviewed, deliberately-HIGH-RISK grants image verification needs — but now in their own clearly-labelled tier, not blended into an opaque bucket. **F-2026-108 (LOW — wrong sudoers path in the trust-model doc)**: `scripts/operator/_action_exec.py`'s "Sudoer strategy" docstring referenced `systemd/sudoers.d/sovereign-os-cockpit`, which does not exist — the reviewed draft lives at `config/sudoers.d/sovereign-os-cockpit` (where `operator-sudoers.sh` + the cockpit lint both read it); a wrong path in the one doc explaining the execution primitive's trust model sends a reviewer to the wrong file. Corrected to `config/sudoers.d/…`. **Verified (real, observed):** `bash -n scripts/operator/operator-sudoers.sh` clean; `operator-sudoers.sh --print` emits the three tiered aliases + the cockpit alias and `visudo -cf` parses OK; `pytest tests/lint/test_operator_sudoers.py tests/lint/test_cockpit_action_exec_sudoers.py` **12 passed** (lockstep reviewed-set + privesc-denylist + tier-separation + the existing not-blanket-ALL / self-validating / make-target checks); `ruff` clean; full `tests/lint` green. 1 sudoers script (tiered `build_body` + `_resolve_bucket`) + 1 lint file (rewritten with lockstep + denylist + tier guards) + 1 docstring path + SDD-700 + INDEX row 700 + F-2026-107..108 ledger + the SDD-100 / docs/sdd/README.md band row for 700–799 + this mandate row — no Rust crate, no gatewayd/cockpit/webapp change; no new dependency; the generated sudoers is unchanged in EFFECT (same commands granted; only split across three named aliases), visudo-valid, install stays self-validating + mode 0440; collision-safe. **Non-goals**: argument-scoping the general-purpose OPS binaries via sudoers wildcards (`mount`/`zfs`/`kill`/`journalctl` are general tools where sudoers arg-wildcards are a known footgun — a badly-scoped wildcard is worse than a documented whole-binary grant; the reviewed lockstep + privesc denylist is the durable guard, and per-verb arg-scoping already exists where safe, the cockpit `sovereign-osctl <verb>` alias); changing which commands are granted (the reviewed set is unchanged; this only guards it); the daemon `NoNewPrivileges=true` vs `sudo` Phase-0-wiring decision. | E11.M999 | **Build-pipeline safety — a missing/critical step must fail the build, not silently pass (SDD-999, F-2026-105..106)** — operator-directed 2026-07-14 (build-and-flash readiness review, **§1g** operator-surface — *"we need to fix everything before I build and flash … the IaC is ready through and through and will be done properly and in proper timing and sequence?"*). **Band 950–999 (phase-1 audit session) per SDD-100.** **Closes F-2026-105 (HIGH) + F-2026-106 (HIGH)** — the second build-and-flash readiness batch (after SDD-998's first-boot ordering). Two build-pipeline scripts could emit a broken image while reporting success. **F-2026-105 (HIGH — orchestrator silent-skip)**: `scripts/build/orchestrate.sh` had an inconsistent dry-run-vs-run contract — `cmd_preflight` (dry-run) treats a missing/non-executable step script as a failure (`return 1` after counting it), but `cmd_run` (the real build) hit the same condition and `log_warn`-skipped it (*"skipping (will land in subsequent PR)"*) + `continue`d, then fell through to `log_info "build pipeline complete"` with success metrics. So a `run` whose `08-image-sign.sh`/`09-image-verify.sh` (or any step) went missing — deleted, un-executable, incomplete checkout — would skip that build stage and still report success, emitting an unsigned/unverified image with no error (the "will land in subsequent PR" wording is a development-era leftover; all nine step scripts now exist). **Fix**: in `cmd_run` a missing/non-executable step is now **fatal** — logs the missing step, refuses to emit an incomplete image, emits the `fail` pipeline metrics, and `exit 1`, matching the dry-run contract; a deliberate partial pipeline during development stays possible via `SOVEREIGN_OS_ALLOW_MISSING_STEPS=1` (records the gap as a failed step + keeps the old skip). **F-2026-106 (HIGH — provision-bake blanket non-fatal)**: `scripts/build/provision-bake.sh` runs `set -uo pipefail` (no `-e`) with every step ending in `|| log …` NON-FATAL BY DESIGN — correct for the many OPTIONAL steps (dashboards, GUI, live-reload, gatewayd, ghostproxy, UPS, node-exporter, config defaults: a hiccup there must never brick the image build, each degrades + recovers post-flash) — but the blanket `exit 0` at the end made even the LOAD-BEARING steps non-fatal: if the operator account couldn't be created, or `systemctl enable sovereign-firstboot.target` failed, provision-bake logged it "(non-fatal)" and the build still succeeded, emitting an image with no operator login or a first boot that runs no hardware setup (the inertness SDD-998 fixed at the unit level, re-introduced if the *enable* silently fails). **Fix** (surgical, NOT a blanket `set -e` which would wrongly make every optional hiccup fatal): a `crit` helper records a failure + increments `_CRIT_FAILURES`; the two image-bricking steps call it — **operator account** (§1: after the useradd block, verify `id "${OPERATOR}"` succeeds — a genuine absence is `crit`) + **first-boot target enable** (§6: on enable failure → `crit`; on success, **verify** the `multi-user.target.wants/sovereign-firstboot.target` symlink actually exists, since an offline `systemctl enable` can no-op silently → a missing symlink is `crit`); the final `exit` is `1` when any critical failure occurred, so the mkosi postinst fails loudly with a summary. Everything else stays non-fatal. **Verified (real, observed):** `bash -n scripts/build/orchestrate.sh scripts/build/provision-bake.sh` both parse clean; `pytest tests/lint/test_build_pipeline_verbatim.py tests/lint/test_shell_safety_flags.py tests/lint/test_graceful_shutdown_contract.py` **32 passed** (verbatim build-pipeline contract + shell-safety + graceful-shutdown all green with the edits); full `tests/lint` green. 2 build scripts + SDD-999 + INDEX row 999 + F-2026-105..106 ledger + this mandate row — no Rust crate, no gatewayd/cockpit/webapp change; no new dependency. All 9 step scripts already exist + the normal bake creates the operator + enables the target cleanly, so the stricter defaults don't break the current build (the VM/emulator path leaves `BAKE_FIRSTBOOT` unset → §6 skipped entirely); collision-safe. **Non-goals**: making the OPTIONAL provisioning steps fatal (non-fatal by design — they degrade + recover post-flash); DKMS-build-failure surfacing inside the driver hook (Batch 3 GPU SDD); re-architecting the step/state/resume model (unchanged — only the missing-step contract moves). | E11.M998 | **First-boot orchestration correctness — the flashed image must actually run its hooks (SDD-998, F-2026-101..104)** — operator-directed 2026-07-14 (build-and-flash readiness review, **§1g** operator-surface — *"we need to fix everything before I build and flash like I said … the IaC is ready through and through and will be done properly and in proper timing and sequence?"*). **Band 950–999 (phase-1 audit session) per SDD-100.** **Closes F-2026-101 (CRIT) + F-2026-102 (HIGH) + F-2026-103 (MED) + F-2026-104 (LOW)** — the first-boot IaC correctness batch of the operator's build-and-flash fix-everything directive. **F-2026-101 (CRIT — the whole flash was inert)**: `systemd/system/sovereign-firstboot.target` groups the 10 first-boot oneshots (network-vlan, nvidia-driver-bind, vfio-bind, zfs-arc-clamp, tetragon-policy-load, warp-setup, ups-setup, workstation-shell-setup, friction-audit, completion marker); the bake + preseed enable **only the target**. But `systemctl enable <target>` never processes the *members'* `[Install] WantedBy=` sections, and `PartOf=` propagates stop/restart only (never start) — so 10 units declared `WantedBy=sovereign-firstboot.target` and **0 were reachable**. On first boot NO hook ran: the flashed SAIN-01 came up as bare Debian (no VLAN/network, no NVIDIA/VFIO bind, no ZFS ARC clamp, no Tetragon policy), and the existing `test_preseed_content_verbatim` stayed green because it only asserted the enable *string* was present, not that first boot did anything. **Fix**: the target now declares `Wants=` for all 10 members (the start-time dependency that enabling the target actually honours); each member still self-gates `ConditionFirstBoot=yes` + `ConditionVirtualization=no`, so this is a no-op on every later boot and on a VM; ordering between members stays their own `After=`; the completion marker is `After=` all of them. **F-2026-102 (HIGH — concurrent initramfs corruption)**: with the members now correctly starting, three of them regenerate the initramfs on first boot (`nvidia-driver-bind.sh` nouveau blacklist, `vfio-bind-4090.sh` vfio-pci early-load, `zfs-arc-clamp.sh` ARC-max option) and their only ordering is `After=sovereign-friction-audit.service` — none relative to each other — so systemd runs up to three `update-initramfs -u` (+ `update-grub`) in parallel, racing on the same `/boot/initrd.img-*` build dir + atomic rename → a truncated initramfs → the box does not boot. **Fix**: a shared `boot_regen()` helper in `scripts/build/lib/common.sh` funnels every boot-config regeneration through one `flock` on `/run/lock/sovereign-os-boot-regen.lock` (serialized one-at-a-time regardless of scheduling; `-w 300` fails a wedged wait rather than hanging first boot forever; runs the command directly if `flock` is absent so a missing lock never means a skipped regen); all three hooks call `boot_regen update-initramfs -u` / `boot_regen update-grub`. **F-2026-103 (MED — no reboot signal for NVIDIA)**: `vfio-bind` writes `/var/lib/sovereign-os/.vfio-bind-needs-reboot` and the completion service prints a `/dev/console` notice for it; `nvidia-driver-bind` did the equivalent boot-affecting work but warned "may need reboot" **only to the journal** (and nouveau may already be bound this boot, so `nvidia-smi` legitimately fails) → the operator sees the VFIO notice and assumes NVIDIA is live when it isn't until the next reboot. **Fix**: the nvidia unit gains `ExecStartPost=/bin/touch /var/lib/sovereign-os/.nvidia-bind-needs-reboot`, and `sovereign-firstboot.service` prints one console notice covering BOTH GPU markers (iterates `.vfio-bind-needs-reboot` + `.nvidia-bind-needs-reboot`) — one reboot brings up both GPUs, and the operator is told so on the console. **F-2026-104 (LOW — guardian mount-order flap)**: the opt-in `sovereign-guardian-core.service` (installed post-deploy by `scripts/auditor/install.sh`, NOT part of the flashed image → not a build blocker) runs `ProtectSystem=strict` with `ReadWritePaths=/mnt/vault/context …` but ordered only `After=tetragon.service`; `/mnt/vault` is a ZFS dataset, so if the daemon starts before the pool mounts, systemd cannot build the mount namespace for that path → `226/NAMESPACE`, and `Restart=always` crash-loops until the pool appears. **Fix**: `After=zfs.target` + `RequiresMountsFor=/mnt/vault/context` + `-`-prefixed ReadWritePaths (tolerate a not-yet-created context/textfile-collector dir at namespace setup). `ExecStart=/usr/local/bin/guardian-core` is **correct and unchanged** — `scripts/auditor/install.sh:59` installs `scripts/auditor/guardian-core.py` there with `install -m 0755` (an earlier "ExecStart broken" hypothesis was disproven by reading the installer). **NEW `tests/lint/test_firstboot_target_membership.py`** (4 cases) makes F-2026-101 un-regressable: the target's `Wants=`/`Upholds=` set must EQUAL the set of units declaring `WantedBy=sovereign-firstboot.target` in both directions (a new hook not wired in, or a dropped member, fails CI) + a floor guard that the hardware/network/security hooks can never quietly fall out of the target. **Verified (real, observed):** `pytest tests/lint/test_firstboot_target_membership.py` **4 passed**; `pytest tests/lint -k "systemd or firstboot or hook or unit or defense or shell"` **1008 passed, 1 skipped** (per-unit systemd coverage + defense-in-depth + hook-hygiene + shell-safety all green with the four edited units + the new `boot_regen` helper + three routed hooks). 4 systemd units + `scripts/build/lib/common.sh` (`boot_regen`) + 3 first-boot hooks + 1 new `tests/lint/` file + SDD-998 + INDEX row 998 + F-2026-101..104 ledger + this mandate row — no Rust crate, no gatewayd/cockpit/webapp change; no new dependency; guardian ExecStart untouched; every on-box change idempotent + `ConditionFirstBoot`-gated where it runs; collision-safe. **Non-goals**: the other readiness batches (GPU driver ≥570/CUDA install hook, GPU power-limit apply-at-boot, inference runtime + model provisioning, sudoers OPS-bucket coverage lint, daemon auth/TLS/timeouts — each its own SDD); wiring the opt-in guardian/tetragon stack into the flashed image (stays a deliberate post-deploy install). | E11.M997 | **Per-crate `✅ integrated` flag on the crate-inventory, validated by named usage (SDD-997, F-2026-100)** — operator-directed 2026-07-14 (phase-1 audit continuation, **§1g** operator-surface — the crate map the operator reads to see what is actually wired). **Band 950–999 (phase-1 audit session) per SDD-100.** **Closes F-2026-100 (LOW).** After SDD-996 flagged which *SDDs* are done, the operator asked the parallel for crates — verbatim: *"were you not suppoed to flag the crates that are done / integrated ?"*. Crate-connection state had been tracked only **negatively / implicitly**: the island register (SDD-955) drains by **removing** a crate's row when it gets wired (so there is no positive record of what IS integrated), and the crate-inventory (SDD-995) bucketed crates by reachability with **no per-crate "integrated" marker** — there was no positive flag, the direct analogue of the SDD `complete` flag. **Operator definition (verbatim)** — where + what it means: *"Flag in crate-inventory"* · *"Production-reachable"* · *"it has to be used to be integrated, not only referenced in a panel"* · *"you can explain the usage to validate the integration"*. So **integrated = actually USED by a running production binary**, not merely referenced (a cockpit crate wasm-bridged for a panel is referenced, not used), and the flag must **explain the usage** that validates it. **Fix**: `scripts/docs/gen-crate-inventory.py` renders a per-crate **✅ integrated** badge for the **57** crates in the dependency closure of the three production binaries (`gatewayd` / `telemetry` / `resource-control` — a crate is integrated only if its code compiles + links into a process that runs); cockpit crates (panel-bridged, SDD-800, 0 panels wired) + demo/hub-only crates are NOT in the closure so are never flagged (directly honouring "used, not merely referenced"). Each badge carries a **usage note** from a new `usage_explanation()` — `runs as a production binary` and/or `used by \`<consumer>\`, …` (the direct production consumers, computed from the reverse dependency edges via a factored-out `direct_deps()`) — e.g. `sovereign-cortex` → *runs as a production binary; used by `sovereign-gatewayd`*; `sovereign-hardware-load-sample` → *used by `sovereign-hardware-dispatch-eligibility`, `sovereign-hardware-thermal-policy`, `sovereign-pressure-reactions`, `sovereign-telemetry`*. | E11.M994 | **The inference router bounds the request body instead of crashing / over-allocating (SDD-994, F-2026-097)** — operator-directed 2026-07-14 (phase-1 audit continuation, *"we continue"*, **§1g** operator-surface — the OpenAI-compatible front door every LM client hits). **Band 950–999 (phase-1 audit session) per SDD-100.** **Closes F-2026-097 (LOW).** `scripts/inference/router.py` `_do_post_inner` read the POST body as `length = int(self.headers.get("Content-Length", 0)); raw = self.rfile.read(length)` — two defects on an untrusted request path: (1) a **non-numeric** `Content-Length` (`Content-Length: abc`) raised an **uncaught `ValueError`** — the exception propagated out of the handler, `BaseHTTPRequestHandler` logged a traceback + dropped the connection; the `0` default covered only an *absent* header, not a *present-but-garbage* one, so a client could spam malformed headers to churn the daemon; (2) `self.rfile.read(length)` trusted the client-declared length with **no cap** — a client claiming `Content-Length: 1099511627776` forced a 1 TiB allocation attempt (memory-DoS). Every sibling operator daemon already guarded both (`control-exec-api.py` `_MAX_BODY = 64*1024` + `length<=0 or >_MAX_BODY → 400`; `code-console-api.py` `length<=0 or >64_000`; `brain-api.py` `try:… except (ValueError, OSError)`) — the router was the lone unguarded body-read. **Fix — one pure, testable helper matched to what the router serves**: `parse_content_length(raw, max_body=_MAX_BODY) -> (length, error)` where `error` is `None` on success else an `(http_status, msg)` the caller sends: absent/empty → `(0, None)` (no body → `json.loads(b"{}")`); non-numeric → `(None, (400, "malformed Content-Length header"))` (was the crash); negative → `(None, (400, …))`; `> max_body` → `(None, (413, "request body exceeds … bytes"))` (was the unbounded read); valid ≤ cap → `(n, None)`. `_do_post_inner` now `length, err = parse_content_length(self.headers.get("Content-Length")); if err is not None: self.send_error(*err); return` **before** `rfile.read(length)`. The cap is a **generous 16 MiB** — the tiny-control APIs cap at 64 KB, but the router proxies *inference* requests where a long-context chat completion is legitimately large; 16 MiB fits very long prompts while keeping the read bounded. Routing (`classify`/`classify_task_type`/`classify_model_class`/`_scheduler_advisory`), metrics + response headers are untouched — this only bounds how the raw bytes are obtained. **NEW `tests/unit/test_router_body_bounds.py`** (11 cases over the pure helper: absent/empty → `(0,None)`; valid + at-cap pass; non-numeric / `12x` whitespace-garbage / negative → `400`; `cap+1` and a `1<<40` (1 TiB) claim → `413` **before any read**; custom `max_body` boundary honored). **Verified (real, observed):** `python3 -m pytest tests/unit/test_router_body_bounds.py tests/unit/test_router_classify.py tests/unit/test_router_scheduler_advisory.py` — **42 passed** (11 new + 31 existing router tests unchanged); `ruff check scripts/inference/router.py tests/unit/test_router_body_bounds.py` — clean. `scripts/inference/router.py` only (1 constant `_MAX_BODY` + 1 pure `parse_content_length` + a 2-line call-site change in `_do_post_inner`) + 1 new `tests/unit/` file + SDD-994 + INDEX row 994 + F-2026-097 ledger entry + this mandate row — no cockpit, no webapp, no crate, no other `scripts/operator` daemon, no new dependency; collision-safe; R10212 (selfdef boundary) / MS043 (offline survivability) untouched. **Non-goals**: a shared `BaseOperatorHandler` unifying the ~58 hand-rolled body-read handlers (a broader refactor — each daemon already guards its own body; this brings the one outlier up to that bar — F-2026-093 island theme); streaming / `Transfer-Encoding: chunked` bodies (the router is request/response JSON); per-deployment cap tuning (a constant now; env-configurable later). MS003 `unsigned-pending-MS003`. | E11.M968 | **Shell-safety-flags contract for entry-point scripts (SDD-968)** — operator-directed 2026-07-13 (*"we continue"*, **§1g** operator-surface — the **CLI**/build shell scripts an operator runs, hardened against silent failure). **Band 950–999 (general/audit session) per SDD-100.** Phase-1 audit; closes ledger **F-2026-024**. The finding flagged "a few scripts lack `set -euo pipefail` without sourcing `common.sh`" (example `scripts/webapp/preflight.sh`) and proposed a targeted sweep — but **investigation showed the premise did not hold as an oversight**: every candidate is a deliberate design or a sourced/staged file. **`scripts/build/provision-bake.sh`** uses `set -uo pipefail` **without `-e` by explicit design** (header: *"NON-FATAL BY DESIGN: `set -uo pipefail` (no -e) and every step ends in…"* — the in-image mkosi postinst provisioner where each step handles its own errors; `-e` would break it). **`scripts/webapp/preflight.sh`** omits `-e` because it is a **fail-counter** — it runs every check, does `fails=$((fails+1))`, and ends `exit "$fails"`; `-e` would abort on the first failing check before the rest run or the count is reported. The remaining candidates are **sourced libraries** (`scripts/build/lib/observability.sh` sourced by 61 callers, `logging.sh`, `runtime-profile.sh`, `selfdef-tune.sh`, `scripts/git-hooks/lib/ownership-warn.sh` whose own header says *"SOURCED, not executed"*) — they run under the caller's shell options and sit beside `common.sh` which already sets `set -euo pipefail`; setting `-e` inside a sourced lib would impose errexit on every caller as a side effect — plus one **operator-neutralized template** (`scripts/claude-code-env/templates/stop-hook-git-check.sh`, re-staged from the read-only image each session). Empirically **0** executable entry-point scripts (excluding libs + templates) ship with *no* safety flags — every one sources `common.sh` or sets at least `set -uo pipefail`. Rather than force `-e` onto scripts that deliberately omit it (which would introduce bugs), this SDD **locks in the good state** with the correct invariant. **NEW `tests/lint/test_shell_safety_flags.py`**: `test_entry_points_opt_into_shell_safety` — every executable `scripts/**/*.sh` **not** under a `lib/` or `templates/` directory must either source `scripts/build/lib/common.sh` or set a shell-safety flag (`set -e` / `set -u` / `set -o pipefail`); requires safety **present** but does **not** mandate `-e` (respecting the two documented non-`-e` designs) — the invariant is "opts into shell safety", not "uses errexit". Guards **91** entry-points; 0 current violations; sourced libs + templates exempt (they run under the caller's options / are staged elsewhere). NEW `docs/sdd/968-shell-safety-flags-contract.md` + INDEX row 968. **Verified:** `provision-bake.sh` carries the "NON-FATAL BY DESIGN" marker; `preflight.sh` has 3 `fails=$((fails+1))` increments + `exit "$fails"`; grep-sweep of executable entry-points (excl lib/templates) with zero safety flags = **0**; `pytest tests/lint/test_shell_safety_flags.py` **2 passed** (91 guarded, 0 violations); `ruff check` clean; full `tests/lint` + `tests/schema` green. **Non-goals**: forcing `set -euo pipefail` (with `-e`) everywhere (two entry points deliberately omit `-e`; the finding's literal wording is superseded by the evidence); adding flags to sourced libraries (they inherit the caller's options — `common.sh` is the deliberate setter); editing the neutralized template (re-staged from the read-only image, a repo edit wouldn't persist). R10212/SB-077 untouched (adds one read-only lint asserting a property the tree already satisfies; changes no script; invents nothing). MS003 `unsigned-pending-MS003`. Status: ✓ shipped this session — the investigation + the shell-safety-flags preserving contract + SDD-968 + INDEX row 968 + this mandate row. | operator-directed 2026-07-13 | SDD-968 (this session) |
| E11.M967 | **Hook hygiene — delete legacy vfio-bind duplicate + executability & dangling-ref contracts (SDD-967)** — operator-directed 2026-07-13 (*"we continue"*, **§1g** operator-surface — the boot-time **hook** dispatch (`scripts/hooks/`) an operator's install runs, its **CLI**/build wiring, and the build-configurator **documentation**). **Band 950–999 (general/audit session) per SDD-100.** Phase-1 audit; closes ledger **F-2026-021** + **F-2026-023** — two ways a hook can silently do the wrong thing. **F-2026-021** (orphaned `vfio-bind-3090.sh`): flagged because its sibling `vfio-bind-4090.sh` is wired into `sovereign-vfio-bind.service` + `config/bootstrap/phases.yaml` + 8 docs while the 3090 was referenced by nothing. Investigation resolved the wire-or-delete ambiguity **decisively**: the two scripts are **byte-identical except the self-naming comment on line 2** (`diff` shows only that line), both read the PCI IDs **from the profile** (no GPU-specific logic — the GPU name lives only in the filename), and the build-configurator's own entry called `vfio-bind-3090` a *"legacy name"* that *"binds the 4090"* — so it is a **legacy-named duplicate to delete**, not a 3090-specific alternative to wire. **Deleted** `scripts/hooks/post-install/vfio-bind-3090.sh` (`git rm`); the canonical profile-driven `vfio-bind-4090.sh` (wired everywhere) is unchanged; its **only** source referrer — the build-configurator step id + description-map key in `webapp/build-configurator/index.html` — was repointed to `vfio-bind-4090` and the "legacy name" wording dropped; `grep -rl vfio-bind-3090` (excl `target/`/`.git/`/ledger) = **0** afterward. **F-2026-023** (glob-dispatch depends on `+x`): `scripts/build/orchestrate.sh` runs pre-install hooks via `find … -type f -executable`, so a hook that loses its executable bit is **silently skipped** with no error. **NEW `tests/lint/test_hook_hygiene.py`**: **`test_all_hooks_executable`** (every `scripts/hooks/**/*.sh` carries its `+x` bit → the glob-dispatch can never silently drop one) + **`test_no_dangling_hook_path_references`** (every `scripts/hooks/**/<name>.sh` PATH in the **dispatch wiring** — `config/bootstrap/phases.yaml` + the systemd units — resolves to a real file; this is exactly the failure the 3090 deletion could have caused, now impossible). **Scope note**: the dangling check covers the wiring surfaces on purpose — prose docs legitimately mention hook paths illustratively (a tutorial `my-hook.sh`), as planned work, or historically (this repo's own findings ledger names the deleted hook), so a docs-wide check would false-positive; a dangling path in the *wiring* is a real install/boot bug, a mention in *docs* is not. The **only** capabilities serve's pipeline has that the daemon still lacks post-206: a **completion cache** (a repeated/paraphrased request costs $0; the daemon re-generates every time) + **token-budget refusal** (a cumulative meter vs the daemon's per-request 1..4096 `max_tokens` clamp); **complexity is superseded** by gatewayd's `sovereign-router-7axis` (complexity is 1 of its 7 routing axes, driving hardware-role routing via the learning Cortex). **Recommendation — Option A**: fold `sovereign-completion-cache` + `sovereign-token-meter` into `generate_chat` via the same `GuardConfig`-as-struct-field insertion pattern SDD-206 established (cache lookup after the injection screen before `resolve_model`; a `TokenMeter` field checked on cache-miss — no `generate_chat` restructuring), **skip** `sovereign-complexity`, then **retire `sovereign-serve`** (delete, or park it in the island register SDD-955 with the trigger "superseded by gatewayd cache+budget"). Rejected: promote-serve (infeasible), keep-both (the two-parallel-orchestrators drift the audit flags), retire-without-fold (loses two real cost-control capabilities). **Sequencing caveat**: the fold edits `generate_chat` + the `GatewayServer` struct — the surface the parallel Anthropic-Messages-API + compute-plane sessions actively touch — so implementation must be **sequenced with them** (or taken by one of them), which is why this is an operator decision, not an immediate PR. | E11.M954 | **Auto-mode permission classifier — flag normalization + honest framing (SDD-954)** — operator-directed 2026-07-12 (*"go"*, **§1g** operator-surface — the permission/approval gate on the `control-exec-api` **service** / execute **API** that fronts the cockpit **Dashboard** controls + CLI). **Band 950–999 (general/audit session) per SDD-100.** Phase-1 audit; closes ledger **F-2026-092**. The Auto-mode safety classifier (`scripts/operator/lib/permission_classifier.py`) had an **evadable `rm` pattern** — a single combined-token regex that only matched recursive+force flags written *together* (`rm -rf`), so `rm -r -f /x` (split) and `rm -R -f /x` (uppercase) **escaped** the `destructive` verdict and fell to `confirm`, undercutting Auto mode's job to block the recursive-delete class — and it was **mis-framed as a boundary** despite being an evadable heuristic denylist. **`permission_classifier.py`**: the two fragile `rm` regexes replaced by `_rm_recursive_or_force(cmd)` — locates any `rm` token (basename match, so `sudo rm …` is covered), scans its option tokens (flag-collection stops at `--`), and flags recursive (`-r`/`-R`/`--recursive`) OR force (`-f`/`--force`) across split / combined / reordered / uppercase / long arrangements → `destructive`; `classify()` consults it before the regex loop. **Tightening-only** (nothing that previously blocked/confirmed becomes allow) with **fail-safe preserved** (unrecognized / quoted / `$IFS`-obfuscated mutations still land in `unknown` → confirm, never a silent allow). The module docstring + the plan-mode/user-approval directive are **reframed**: the classifier is a **best-effort UX heuristic, NOT a security boundary** — it reduces footguns for a cooperative caller, it does not contain an adversary; the ACTUAL boundary is the allowlisted execute daemon (`control-exec-api`: allowlisted control-id + dry-run default + audit) plus the fs sandbox around the execution paths (F-2026-081); a `block` reads as "spared the operator a likely mistake", never "an attacker was stopped". NEW `docs/sdd/954-permission-classifier-flag-normalization.md` + INDEX row 954. **Verified:** `python3 -m pytest tests/lint/test_plan_mode_contract.py` 7 (2 new — every recursive/force `rm` arrangement `-rf`/`-r -f`/`-R -f`/`-fr`/`-Rf`/`--recursive --force`/`-r`/`--force`/`sudo rm -r -f` → destructive → block under Auto; plain `rm file.txt` → unknown → confirm, fail-safe not fail-open; the module + directive assert best-effort-not-boundary framing); `ruff check scripts/operator/lib/permission_classifier.py` clean; full `tests/lint` + `tests/schema` green. **Non-goals**: defeating quoting / `$IFS` / base64 obfuscation (a regex classifier can't, and the fail-safe → confirm direction already prevents silent-allow); the real execution-path boundary = sandbox-profile / fs-boundary enforcement (F-2026-081), which this SDD makes the classifier honest about being the UX layer on top of. | E11.M951 | **Durable memory — never silently lost: corruption recovery + bounded growth (SDD-951)** — operator-directed 2026-07-12 (*"continue"*, **§1g** operator-surface / **§4** safety — the gateway **service** + **API**'s learned recall). **Band 950–999 (general/audit session) per SDD-100.** Phase-1 audit; closes ledger **F-2026-084** *partially* (corruption-recovery + bounded-growth; the decay half deferred). The gateway daemon (`sovereign-gatewayd` **service**, the box's local AI **API** backend) persists its learning Cortex's `MemoryStore` to `SOVEREIGN_GATEWAY_MEMORY` on a timer so recall survives a restart — but the load was `serde_json::from_str(&json).unwrap_or_else(seed_memory)`: **any** parse failure (a torn file from a hard kill, a manual edit, a struct-shape change across versions) **silently discarded ALL learned memory** and reseeded with no signal; and the store grew **unbounded** (re-serialized whole every ~10s snapshot). **`sovereign-memory-os`**: NEW `MemoryStore::set_capacity(Option<usize>)` — sets/clears the bound and immediately evicts the lowest-value residents down to it (value-based via the existing `evict_lowest_value`; ties → oldest freshness → lowest id; **no wall-clock, can never over-evict** — the property that makes it safe to add now, unlike time-decay) + a `capacity()` getter. **`sovereign-gatewayd`**: NEW pure `load_memory_from(path) -> (MemoryStore, MemoryLoadOutcome)` — absent ⇒ Fresh (seed); valid ⇒ Loaded; **unparseable ⇒ move the file aside to `<path>.corrupt` (atomic rename) + reseed** ⇒ Recovered — the old bytes **preserved for forensic recovery, never discarded**, logged loudly; `with_force_local` uses it, logs the outcome (resumed N items / recovered+backed-up / fresh), then caps via `set_capacity(memory_capacity_from_env())`. NEW env `SOVEREIGN_GATEWAY_MEMORY_CAP` (default 4096, `0`=unbounded). **Backward-compatible on-disk format** (still a raw `MemoryStore` JSON; `capacity` is `#[serde(default)]` so old files load); **zero behaviour change when `SOVEREIGN_GATEWAY_MEMORY` unset** (the common test/dev path). NEW `docs/sdd/951-durable-memory-corruption-safety.md` + INDEX row 901. **Verified:** `cargo test -p sovereign-memory-os` 40 (2 new — set_capacity bounds a previously-unbounded store + stays bounded; None removes the bound) + `-p sovereign-gatewayd` lib 55 (4 new — absent ⇒ fresh seed; valid store round-trips; **corruption ⇒ reseed + `.corrupt` backup preserved + original moved aside + bytes recoverable**; cap env default finite) + main 4 + transports 14; `cargo clippy -p sovereign-gatewayd -p sovereign-memory-os --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean; downstream cortex/serve build unchanged; `cargo fmt --all --check` clean. **Deferred (Q-901-001)**: the M028 decay pass (`GatewayServer::maintain`) exists but is unscheduled — wiring it needs a unified monotonic admission clock first (today request `now` is ad-hoc — `0` from SimpleRequest, `100` from CoAT — so a decay thread on an independent clock could age everything or nothing; a wrong decay is worse than none). Bounded growth already caps the accumulation symptom clock-independently. R10212/SB-077 untouched (additive; corruption path preserves state, never fabricates). MS003 `unsigned-pending-MS003`. | E11.M950 | **Real RoPE — `rope_theta` + `rope_scaling` from the model config (SDD-950)** — operator-directed 2026-07-12 (*"we continue"*, **§1a** intelligence-substrate). **Number band 950–999 (general/audit session) per SDD-100** — this session works in its own reserved band so it can never collide with the recover / header-sidemenu / science-tools sessions (the SDD-206/207 collision this session helped cause was exactly the failure the bands prevent; lesson taken). Arc 1 of the Phase-1 whole-repo audit (`docs/review/phase-1/99-findings-ledger.md`), closing ledger **F-2026-080**. Every decoder block was built with `Rope::new(head_dim)` — a **hardcoded RoPE frequency base of 10000** — so Llama-3 (trained base 500000), Qwen2 (1000000), Mistral etc. decoded as **garbage** (every position rotated at the wrong frequency). THE single biggest blocker to running a real model, and it directly undercut SDD-205 (the Anthropic-compatible gateway **API** — `/v1/messages` + the OpenAI shim — returning garbage is unusable from VS Code / Claude Code; this fix is what makes that operator-facing API surface actually coherent). Pure plumbing — `sovereign-rope` already carried `with_base` / `ntk_aware_base` / `with_yarn`; they were never fed the config's real values. **`sovereign-mha-block`**: NEW `MhaDecoderBlock::with_rope(theta_base, scaling)` builder (mirrors `with_context_extension`; **additive** — the 8 `MhaBlockWeights` construction sites + all existing tests untouched) + NEW public `RopeScalingKind` (Linear / Dynamic / Yarn / Llama3) + `RopeScaling`, mapping onto sovereign-rope: none → `with_base(theta)`, linear → `position_scale = 1/factor`, dynamic → `ntk_aware_base`, yarn → `with_yarn` when `original_ctx` is known (else honest base-only fallback), llama3 → exact base (short-context coherent; the low/high-freq ramp a noted follow-up). **`sovereign-safetensors-loader`**: `Config` gains `rope_theta` (serde default 10000) + `rope_scaling` (accepts both newer `rope_type` + older `type`; factor / `original_max_position_embeddings` / beta_fast / beta_slow); `rope_scaling_resolved()` (unrecognized type ⇒ `None`, base-theta only — never a fabricated scaling, never a parse failure); every block built `.with_rope(config.rope_theta, config.rope_scaling_resolved().as_ref())`; the stale "Out: non-default rope_theta" doc-limitation replaced with the "In" note. **Honest per SB-077**: apply what sovereign-rope models exactly, fall back to the correct base theta (the dominant correctness win) for what it doesn't yet model, and say so. NEW `docs/sdd/950-real-rope-theta-scaling.md` + INDEX row 900. **Verified**: `cargo test -p sovereign-mha-block` 28 (8 new — default base 10000; `with_rope` sets base; linear ⇒ position_scale = 1/factor; dynamic ⇒ base raised; YaRN engages with known ctx / honest fallback without; llama3 base-only; **a distinct RoPE base yields distinct decode output** — proving the head is wired, not a no-op field) + `-p sovereign-safetensors-loader` 13 (6 new — theta default/parse; linear via `type`; llama3 via `rope_type` + original_ctx; yarn betas; unknown type ⇒ no-scaling-not-error); `cargo clippy -p sovereign-mha-block -p sovereign-safetensors-loader --all-targets -- -D warnings` clean; downstream quant-llm / gatewayd / decoder-layer / inference-demo build unchanged; `cargo fmt --all --check` clean. **Non-goals (next arcs)**: sampling params + chat template (F-2026-086 — inherently touches the gateway generation signature the parallel Anthropic session is editing; scoped next to avoid collision); GGUF / quantized weight loading (F-2026-085); the llama3 freq ramp (Q-900-001); real-model coherence (no weights / no network in this environment — the *machinery* lands + is unit-tested, and a real Llama-3 config now threads the right base end-to-end). R10212/SB-077 untouched (additive config plumbing; guard-free math path unchanged). MS003 `unsigned-pending-MS003`. | E11.M501 | **Multi-plane token-law composition — gate the decoder by grammar AND policy at once (SDD-501)** — operator-directed 2026-07-21 (*"Good, we continue, another big PR"* → chose *"Multi-plane token-law (M00117)"*). | E11.M502 | **Incremental Earley parser — per-token grammar masking without re-parsing the prefix (SDD-502)** — operator-directed 2026-07-21 (*"Good, we continue, another big PR"* → chose *"Incremental grammar parser"*). The third SDD in the control-bits band (500–599); closes the honest-perf caveat SDD-500 AND SDD-501 both flagged verbatim (*"`TokenGrammarMask::mask` re-parses the whole prefix each step … the dominant per-token cost"*). GROUNDED: `sovereign-cfg-grammar`'s `parse_chart` rebuilds a fresh Earley chart on EVERY call, and `TokenGrammarMask::mask` calls `is_live_prefix(prefix+token)` for every surviving token — ≈ O(S·L·G) per step, quadratic across a generation (the biggest cost in every grammar-constrained path: `complete_json_schema` / `complete_regex` / SDD-501's `complete_json_schema_with_laws`). KEY PROPERTY exploited: the Earley chart is a PURE function of the prefix — building state k+1 only appends it and never mutates 0..=k (scan reads S[k]; predict/complete write only the new state) — so a committed prefix parses ONCE and each candidate token is validated by feed-then-rollback (cost ∝ token length, not prefix length), bit-for-bit identical to the from-scratch recognizer (the same predict/scan/complete, persisted). Ships (**NO new crate** — 722 unchanged): a public `EarleyChart` + `Grammar::start_chart`/`feed`/`feed_str`/`rollback_to`/`next_set`/`is_live`/`accepts` in `sovereign-cfg-grammar` (the from-scratch `allowed_next`/`is_live_prefix`/`accepts` stay UNCHANGED as the parity oracle); `TokenGrammarMask::mask` rewired to the within-call incremental path — a **drop-in** with the identical signature+output, so EVERY caller inherits the speedup with zero code change (per-step O(S·L·G)→O(L·G + S·t·G), removing the survivors×prefix-length blow-up); and a stateful `IncrementalGrammarMask` that persists the committed chart across steps (`advance`/`advance_token`/`mask`/`eos_allowed`) → **linear** per generation (O(new_chars·G + S·t·G)). **Honest boundary:** the stateful masker is CHARACTER-domain and requires a char-concatenative tokenizer (`decode(a)+decode(b)==decode([a,b])` — byte-BPE satisfies it, merge-BPE generally not), so it ships as a substrate; the LLM wiring keeps the stateless drop-in `mask` (also incremental, per-call, no concatenation assumption) — mirroring the SDD-500/501 honest-boundary doctrine. Complexity not micro-opt: no SIMD, no `unsafe` (`forbid(unsafe_code)` holds in both crates); parity is the acceptance test (unchanged `prefilter_matches_full_check` + new `EarleyChart`-vs-from-scratch parity tests over balanced/number/expr incl. dead ends + speculative-feed-then-rollback restore). **Status: v1 shipped 2026-07-21** (code complete; lands as a draft PR for operator review per E0634). Verified: `cargo test -p sovereign-cfg-grammar -p sovereign-token-grammar-mask` (14+14 pass) + all downstream green (`sovereign-llm` 79 lib + 28 runtime, `sovereign-json-schema-grammar` 13, `sovereign-token-law-mask` 9, `sovereign-decoder-stack` 37 — exact parity inherited); clippy `-D warnings` + fmt clean; `tests/lint/test_incremental_grammar_parser_contract.py` locks the append-only contract + the char-concatenative caveat. Future (tracked): a bitset-per-state SIMD chart representation; wiring the stateful path into the byte-BPE decode loop. Lands (SDD-502 active + INDEX row 502 + this mandate row + catalog regen + context sdd count 211→212). | operator-directed 2026-07-21 | SDD-502 (control-bits session) |

| E11.M504 | **Safety denylist as a negative-constraint token-law plane (SDD-504)** — operator-directed 2026-07-21 (*"Good, we continue, another big PR"*). The fifth SDD in the control-bits band (500–599); ships the source SDD-503 explicitly deferred (§Non-goals #1: *"a safety-denylist plane (substring bans are not per-token — needs a new text→token projection, a separate design)"*), completing the M00117 five-plane vision (grammar · schema · tool · SAFETY · route). Every constraint 500–503 is a POSITIVE allow-list ("the next token must keep some pattern reachable"); safety is the opposite — "the output must NEVER contain any of these substrings" (prompt-injection markers, banned phrases) — a NEGATIVE constraint. THE CRUX (why 503 deferred it): a substring ban is NOT a per-token property — a forbidden phrase can span token boundaries, so with a byte-level tokenizer "ab" is the token `a` then the token `b` and NEITHER contains "ab"; banning either token is both wrong and insufficient. REALIZATION: compile the denied substrings into an Aho-Corasick automaton, walk it over the committed generation to a scan state, then each step ban exactly the tokens whose bytes would COMPLETE a banned match — `DenyConstraint::safe_token_ids(generated, vocab) -> Vec<usize>` returns the safe allow-list (the SAME shape `sovereign-regex-constrain`/`TokenLawPlanes` consume, so a safety plane composes with grammar/regex/policy through the M00117 `token_law_combine`). The guarantee is EXACT and per-step (a banned phrase can only appear at the byte that finishes it, and that token is masked at that step) — a decode-time guarantee, NOT a post-hoc scanner. Ships: `AcState` + `start`/`advance`/`hits` incremental scan-state API on `sovereign-aho-corasick` (its `step(state,byte)` was private — only whole-haystack scans were public; the additive `Copy` state lets a decode loop probe a candidate from a committed state without re-scanning the prefix, no rollback); **NEW crate `sovereign-token-law-deny`** (722→723) — `DenyConstraint`/`safe_token_ids`/`is_denied`, `forbid(unsafe_code)`, mirroring `RegexConstraint::allowed_token_ids`; `complete_with_safety_denylist` (pure negative) + `complete_regex_with_safety_denylist` (a POSITIVE plane (regex) AND a NEGATIVE plane (denylist) at once via `combine_with_dynamics` — a composition no single constraint expresses) in `sovereign-llm`. REAL source: the wiring consumes `sovereign_injection_detect::PATTERNS` (24 literal injection phrases) verbatim, output guaranteed clean. **Honest boundary:** structural detectors — `sovereign-secret-scan` (Shannon-entropy thresholds) and `sovereign-pii-redact` (Luhn checksums / shape rules) — are NOT literal substrings and "the token that completes a high-entropy secret" is not well-defined, so they stay POST-HOC SCANNERS, NOT planes (deliberately out of scope, matching 503's honesty about what is and isn't a plane). Only literal-substring denylists (injection phrases, banned terms) become a plane. **Status: v1 shipped 2026-07-21** (code complete; lands as a draft PR for operator review per E0634). Verified: `cargo test -p sovereign-aho-corasick -p sovereign-token-law-deny -p sovereign-llm` (12 + 8 + 86 lib + 28 runtime pass — incl. the DETERMINISTIC cross-token proofs: forbidden "ab" → after committed "a", token "b"/"bc" banned, "x" safe; a token whose own bytes contain "ab" banned; single-byte ban excludes any token containing it; overlapping "he"/"she"; plus end-to-end: ban byte `a` → no `a`; regex `[a-z]+` ∧ deny `z` → a–y; the real `injection_detect::PATTERNS` source → output clean) + the new-crate registration lints green (crate-inventory regenerated — NON-integrated, reached via the `sovereign-llm` hub; crate-graph reachable via `sovereign-llm`, no orphan; rustdoc-panel catalog 722→723; context workspace-crates 722→723); clippy `-D warnings` + fmt clean; `tests/lint/test_safety_denylist_plane_contract.py` locks the incremental automaton API + the negative-plane crate + the wiring + the structural-detectors-are-not-planes boundary. Future (tracked): negated-regex denials (a forbidden *pattern*, not a literal substring); the M00155 operator surface (`--token-law-mask-layers`, `POST /v1/data-plane/token-law/fuse`). Lands (SDD-504 active + INDEX row 504 + this mandate row + catalog regen + context sdd count 213→214 + workspace-crates 722→723). | operator-directed 2026-07-21 | SDD-504 (control-bits session) |
| E11.M505 | **The unified token-law engine — one declarative spec composing all M00117 planes (SDD-505)** — operator-directed 2026-07-21 (*"Good, we continue, another big PR"*). The sixth SDD in the control-bits band (500–599); the CAPSTONE that folds the five plane classes built plane-by-plane in SDD-500…504 (per-token mask / multi-plane composition / incremental parser / real positive sources regex+tool / negative safety source) into ONE declarative entry point. The LLM surface had accreted as FIVE pairwise methods (`complete_json_schema_with_laws`, `complete_regex_with_laws`, `complete_json_schema_and_regex_with_laws`, `complete_with_safety_denylist`, `complete_regex_with_safety_denylist`) — a combinatorial explosion that STILL could not express "grammar ∧ regex ∧ safety ∧ policy all at once." GENUINELY-NEW: composes ALL plane types simultaneously (no method did more than two). Ships (**NO new crate** — 723 unchanged; no new dependency — all plane crates already in `sovereign-llm`): `TokenLawSpec<'a>` (`Debug + Clone + Default`, `is_empty`) — a declarative plane set: `schema: Option<&Schema>` grammar plane (stop on completion) / `regex: Option<&str>` regex plane (tool-name = `(a|b|…)` alternation) / `denylist: &[&str]` negative safety plane / `policy_planes: &[&[u64]]` static allow-bitsets; `Default` = the empty (unconstrained) spec; `SovereignLlm::complete_with_token_law(prompt, spec, max_new, seed)` builds each active constraint once then per decode step collects EVERY active dynamic plane's allow-list and calls `TokenLawPlanes::combine_with_dynamics` — the real `token_law_combine` And over all dynamics AND the static policy planes — so a token survives only if every active plane allows it; stops on grammar `eos` / an empty plane / an empty intersection; an empty spec runs unconstrained to `max_new`. FAITHFUL GENERALIZATION (parity is the proof): because `combine_with(x) ≡ combine_with_dynamics(&[x])` (SDD-503), a single-plane spec produces the BIT-FOR-BIT identical mask — and identical output — as the corresponding dedicated method; the five pairwise methods are RETAINED (back-compat), the engine is a strict superset verified by parity tests, not a replacement that risks drift. Also the clean CODE SUBSTRATE the spec'd M00155 `--token-law-mask-layers grammar,schema,tool,safety` operator surface needs (the CSV layer list maps directly onto the spec's fields). **Status: v1 shipped 2026-07-21** (code complete; lands as a draft PR for operator review per E0634). Future (tracked): the M00155 CLI/HTTP/dashboard operator surface over this engine; a negated-regex denial plane (SDD-504's tracked future). | E11.M506 | **The negated-regex denial plane — forbid the output from matching a pattern (SDD-506)** — operator-directed 2026-07-21 (*"ready for the next big PR"*). SDD-504's OWN tracked future (§Non-goals: *"negated-regex denials — a forbidden pattern, not a literal substring"*), the seventh SDD in the control-bits band (500–599). Where SDD-503's `regex` plane forces output ONTO a pattern (positive), this keeps it OFF one (NEGATIVE): the output must NEVER MATCH the forbidden regex anywhere (an SSN shape `\d\d\d-\d\d-\d\d\d\d`, a banned id format). THE CRUX (why it's genuinely-new engine work, not exposure): "match anywhere" needs an UNANCHORED NFA — `sovereign-regex-nfa` was anchored at both ends (`is_match` requires the whole string to match); the standard Thompson trick is to simulate the NFA with the START STATE ALWAYS ACTIVE — re-seed the start closure at every position so a match may begin there, and an accepting live set means a substring match ended at the current character. Like SDD-504 a forbidden match can span token boundaries, so it is detected at the character that COMPLETES it — an exact per-step guarantee (a forbidden match can only appear at the char that finishes it, and that token is masked at that step), NOT a post-hoc scanner. Ships (**NO new crate** — the negative plane lives BESIDE the positive `RegexConstraint`, same NFA substrate, so no crate-count change): `start_unanchored`/`step_unanchored`/`matches_anywhere` on `sovereign-regex-nfa` (additive; anchored `is_match`/`step` unchanged; union of two epsilon-closed sets is itself closed, so no re-closure); `RegexDenyConstraint` (`new`/`from_regex`/`regex`/`is_denied`/`safe_token_ids` — mirrors `RegexConstraint::allowed_token_ids`, returns the safe allow-list a token-law plane consumes) on `sovereign-regex-constrain`; and `TokenLawSpec::regex_denylist: &[&str]` + composition in `complete_with_token_law` (the SDD-505 unified engine — builds a `RegexDenyConstraint` per pattern, AND-composes each safe-set with the other planes via `combine_with_dynamics`), so a model can be confined by grammar ∧ positive-regex ∧ literal-denylist ∧ NEGATED-regex ∧ policy simultaneously; `TokenLawSpec::is_empty` accounts for the new field, the SDD-505 parity tests unaffected (field defaults to empty). **Honest boundary:** patterns matching the EMPTY string forbid everything (documented, not special-cased); the NFA feature set only (`* + ? | () . [] \d \w \s`, no `{n}` bounds / backrefs / lookaround). **Status: v1 shipped 2026-07-21** (code complete; lands as a draft PR for operator review per E0634). Verified: `cargo test -p sovereign-regex-nfa -p sovereign-regex-constrain -p sovereign-llm` (14 + 13 + 92 lib + 28 runtime pass) — incl. DETERMINISTIC cross-token proofs (forbidden `ab`: after committed `a`, token `b`/`bc` banned, `x` safe; a token whose own chars are two digits banned for `\d\d`; a cross-token digit pair `1`+`2`; `cat|dog` matched mid-token in `xdogy`) + the unanchored-NFA unit tests (substring finds; is_accepting flips exactly when a match completes mid-stream) + end-to-end (positive `[a-z]+` ∧ negated `[xyz]` → lowercase a–w only, a regex CLASS the literal denylist can't express); clippy `-D warnings` + fmt clean; `tests/lint/test_negated_regex_denial_plane_contract.py` locks the unanchored API + the negative-regex constraint + the engine field + the empty-match caveat. Future (tracked): the M00155 CLI/HTTP/dashboard operator surface. Lands (SDD-506 active + INDEX row 506 + this mandate row + catalog regen + context sdd count 215→216; NO new crate — crate count unchanged). | operator-directed 2026-07-21 | SDD-506 (control-bits session) |
| E11.M507 | **The token-law fusion data plane — expose the engine's decision as a checkpoint-free surface (SDD-507)** — operator-directed 2026-07-21 (*"what the progress and what next? I want vision"* → chose ALL of Expose · Connect · Deepen). The eighth SDD in the control-bits band (500–599); the FIRST of the **Expose** arc. SDD-500…506 built the complete M00117 five-plane engine but left it **SEALED** — `complete_with_token_law` had ZERO callers outside its own tests; no osctl verb, no HTTP path, no dashboard drove it (empirically verified: whole-repo grep for `complete_with_token_law`/`TokenLawSpec` hit only the defining crate + its tests + the SDDs). This opens the spec'd-but-unbuilt M00155 operator surface (`backlog/milestones/M010-deterministic-data-plane.md`, F00792 fusion engine / F00797 `POST /v1/data-plane/token-law/fuse` / F00798 metric). **THE HONESTY INSIGHT** (why this is the right first slice): the engine's per-step DECISION — the fused allow-mask — is a PURE FUNCTION of the layer SOURCES (a JSON schema, a regex, a denylist) + the vocabulary STRINGS; it never touches embeddings, attention, or logits. So the mask is EXACT regardless of which checkpoint is loaded, or whether ANY is — a trained model, the untrained in-repo fixture (`crates/sovereign-gatewayd/src/model_fixture.rs`, deterministic-pseudo-random weights), and "no model, just a tokenizer" all produce the IDENTICAL mask. That is what makes the operator surface honest: you can inspect + drive the law engine without a trained model behind it. (Contrast: exposing GENERATION would be architecturally-real but untrained-gibberish out of the box — a separate, larger surface deferred to Connect.) THE CRUX: `complete_with_token_law` interleaved (1) FUSE the active laws at a prefix into an allow-mask and (2) SAMPLE the transformer under it; only (2) needs the model. This SDD extracts (1) into a crate depending on the constraint SOURCES only — NO `sovereign-decoder-stack`, no transformer-block — so a LIGHT consumer (the gateway daemon, `/metrics`, a future CLI) computes masks without linking a decode stack; and because generation + inspection now call the SAME `fused_mask`, they can never diverge (bit-for-bit the mask the decoder applies). Ships: **NEW crate `sovereign-token-law-fuse`** (725→726) — `FuseLayers` (borrowed named laws) / `CompiledFuse::compile` + `fused_mask(generated) -> FusedMask{mask,allowed,per_layer,stop}` (allow-count is vocab-bounded — the identity mask sets padding bits past the vocab, the mask itself returned verbatim) / `FuseError` / owned `Deserialize` `FuseRequest` (`{schema?,regex?,denylist?,regex_denylist?,policy_planes?,generated?,vocab}` + `fuse()` + `layers_active()`), deps the sources only, `forbid(unsafe_code)`; `sovereign-llm::complete_with_token_law` refactored to build a `CompiledFuse` once + call `fused_mask` per step (behaviour UNCHANGED — the five pairwise methods + all SDD-505/506 parity tests untouched); `POST /v1/data-plane/token-law/fuse` on `sovereign-gatewayd` (a LIGHT dep) that DERIVES each named layer's bitset from a real source (unlike the pre-packed-bitset `/v1/token-law/allowed-mask`), reply `{kind,mask,allowed_tokens,per_layer,layers_active,stop}`, + the `sovereign_data_plane_token_law_mask_layers` counter metric (F00798, `record_token_law_fuse`). **ESTABLISHES THE 3-FORK ROADMAP** (operator chose all three): (1) Expose — this crate+route → the `--token-law-mask-layers` osctl verb + profile knob + env (F00793/4/5) → the dashboard heatmap (F00796); (2) Connect — cross the `/v1/messages` no-logit-access boundary (production serving proxies out-of-process; gatewayd self-generates on a DIFFERENT stack `sovereign-quant-model` than the engine's `sovereign-llm`/`DecoderStack`) so the engine constrains REAL traffic; (3) Deepen — the "route" plane as a real source + a text→token projection for the entropy/checksum safety detectors + SIMD to hit the 16 KB / AVX-512 target. **Status: v1 shipped 2026-07-21** (code complete; lands as a draft PR for operator review per E0634). Verified: `cargo test -p sovereign-token-law-fuse -p sovereign-llm -p sovereign-gatewayd` (8 + 92 lib + 28 runtime + 119 + 25 + 21 pass — incl. the fuse crate's identity/positive-regex/positive∧negated/cross-boundary-denylist/policy-AND/empty-intersection-stop/invalid-regex/JSON-round-trip proofs + the route deriving+counting named layers on `/metrics` + 400 on empty-vocab/bad-regex); clippy `-D warnings` + fmt clean; new-crate registration lints green (crate-inventory NON-integrated reached via `sovereign-llm`+`sovereign-gatewayd`, crate-graph reachable, rustdoc-panel 725→726, context workspace-crates 725→726); `tests/lint/test_token_law_fusion_data_plane_contract.py` locks the checkpoint-free crate + the llm delegation + the route/metric + the honest checkpoint-independence framing. | E11.M149 | **dashboard serve.py `--once` — fix the empty-reply race (SDD-149)** — `tests/nspawn/test_dashboard.sh` failed 2/33 (`curl GET /` + `GET /api/health` → **rc=52 empty reply**) → CI **layer-3 nspawn gate** red on PR #118. Deterministic + pre-existing on `main`, **masked** until SDD-148 fixed `test_trinity` (the layer-3 job stops at the first failing test; trinity failed first so dashboard never ran). **§1g** operator-surface. Operator: "still failing" (re-sent the dashboard failure). Recover band (SDD-149/E11.M149 per SDD-100). **Root cause**: `serve.py` runs on `ThreadingHTTPServer`; for `--once` it calls `handle_request()`, which **dispatches the request to a worker thread and returns as soon as the thread is spawned — NOT when the response is written**; `ThreadingHTTPServer` workers are **daemons by default**, so `main()` reaching `finally: server_close()` + returning **kills the worker mid-render** before it flushes → empty reply. Deterministic because the full-page render (`gather_all` ~40 cards, 3-4s) is always still in flight; auth passes on loopback (not involved); `--render-only` always worked (no server, direct render — which is why the bug hid behind the HTTP path only). **Fix**: in the `--once` branch set `srv.daemon_threads=False` so `server_close()` (`ThreadingMixIn.block_on_close`, default True) **joins** the worker and the response completes before exit; the normal `serve_forever()` path is untouched (keeps running, daemon workers finish naturally). **Serving-lifecycle only** — no route/data/auth/render change; R10212/SB-077 untouched. Verified: `test_dashboard.sh` **35/35** (was 31/33; the success-path follow-on assertions now run too), 3/3 consecutive runs, 0 curl fails; all 7 dashboard nspawn suites green (`_auth` 14/14, `_grid` 21/21, `_intel_cards` 10/10, `_mobile` 10/10, `_model_detail` 13/13, `_modules_form` 0-fail — the 3 exercising the `--once` HTTP path all pass); full pytest lint suite green. MS003 `unsigned-pending-MS003`. Status: SDD-149 shipped on branch (stacked with SDD-147/148 on PR #118). | operator-directed 2026-07-11 | SDD-149 on branch `claude/recover-projects-b0oT6` |

## 4. How future rounds use this file

1. **Pick the next TODO Module** from any Epic above. Prefer Modules
   whose Epic has the most TODO siblings (broaden coverage) or the
   Module that unblocks downstream work.
2. **Decompose into rounds.** A Module may need 1-10 rounds. Each
   round = one round-ID (R<N> or SD-R<N>) + commit + push.
3. **Cite Epic / Module ID in commit message** (e.g. "Round 265 —
   heat-budget integration (E1.M11)"). This is the structural trace
   that addresses the operator's "make sure we record this and make
   sure we do some things about it" mandate.
4. **Update THIS FILE** when a Module flips to ✓. New TODO Modules
   added under existing Epics MUST quote the operator's verbatim
   text they derive from.

## 5. What this file does NOT do

This file is the **decomposition** of the mandate, not the
**implementation status**. SDD-029 + each round's L3 test are the
implementation truth. INDEX.md remains the chronological SDD ledger.
Handoff docs remain the trajectory tracker.

## 6. Anti-corruption invariants

- Do **NOT** rewrite the operator's verbatim text. Edits to Section 1
  require a new file with a new date and operator confirmation.
- Do **NOT** delete TODO Modules without operator confirmation.
- New Modules added during work go under an Epic with a one-line
  source-quote citation.
